Nisajja kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘tasmātiha, bhikkhave, ye te mayā dhammā abhiññā desitā, te vo sādhukaṃ uggahetvā āsevitabbā bhāvetabbā bahulīkātabbā, yathayidaṃ brahmacariyaṃ addhaniyaṃ assa ciraṭṭhitikaṃ, tadassa bahujanahitāya bahujanasukhāya lokānukampāya atthāya hitāya sukhāya devamanussānaṃ. Katame ca te, bhikkhave, dhammā mayā abhiññā desitā, ye vo sādhukaṃ uggahetvā āsevitabbā bhāvetabbā bahulīkātabbā, yathayidaṃ brahmacariyaṃ addhaniyaṃ assa ciraṭṭhitikaṃ, tadassa bahujanahitāya bahujanasukhāya lokānukampāya atthāya hitāya sukhāya devamanussānaṃ. Seyyathidaṃ – cattāro satipaṭṭhānā cattāro sammappadhānā cattāro iddhipādā pañcindriyāni pañca balāni satta bojjhaṅgā ariyo aṭṭhaṅgiko maggo. Ime kho te, bhikkhave, dhammā mayā abhiññā desitā, ye vo sādhukaṃ uggahetvā āsevitabbā bhāvetabbā bahulīkātabbā, yathayidaṃ brahmacariyaṃ addhaniyaṃ assa ciraṭṭhitikaṃ, tadassa bahujanahitāya bahujanasukhāya lokānukampāya atthāya hitāya sukhāya devamanussāna’’nti.

184.Then the Blessed One went to the service hall, sat down on the prepared seat, and addressed the monks: "Therefore, monks, those teachings I have directly known and taught—you should thoroughly learn them, cultivate them, develop them, and frequently practice them, so that this holy life may endure long, for the welfare and happiness of many people, out of compassion for the world, for the benefit, welfare, and happiness of gods and humans. And what are those teachings I have directly known and taught? They are the four foundations of mindfulness, the four right exertions, the four bases of spiritual power, the five faculties, the five powers, the seven factors of enlightenment, and the Noble Eightfold Path. These, monks, are the teachings I have directly known and taught—you should thoroughly learn them, cultivate them, develop them, and frequently practice them, so that this holy life may endure long, for the welfare and happiness of many people, out of compassion for the world, for the benefit, welfare, and happiness of gods and humans."

185. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘handadāni, bhikkhave, āmantayāmi vo, vayadhammā saṅkhārā, appamādena sampādetha. Naciraṃ tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Ito tiṇṇaṃ māsānaṃ accayena tathāgato parinibbāyissatī’’ti. Idamavoca bhagavā, idaṃ vatvāna sugato athāparaṃ etadavoca satthā [ito paraṃ syāmapotthake evaṃpi pāṭho dissati –§daharāpi ca ye vuddhā, ye bālā ye ca paṇḍitā.§aḍḍhāceva daliddā ca, sabbe maccuparāyanā.§yathāpi kumbhakārassa, kataṃ mattikabhājanaṃ.§khuddakañca mahantañca, yañca pakkaṃ yañca āmakaṃ.§sabbaṃ bhedapariyantaṃ, evaṃ maccāna jīvitaṃ.§athāparaṃ etadavoca satthā]. –

185.Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: "Now, monks, I declare to you: all conditioned things are subject to decay; strive on with diligence. The Tathāgata's final passing will be soon. Three months from now, the Tathāgata will attain final Nibbāna." This the Blessed One said. Having said this, the Fortunate One, the Teacher, further said:

‘‘Paripakko vayo mayhaṃ, parittaṃ mama jīvitaṃ;Pahāya vo gamissāmi, kataṃ me saraṇamattano.

"My age is advanced, my life is limited; Forsaking you, I shall depart, having made myself my refuge."

‘‘Appamattā satīmanto, susīlā hotha bhikkhavo;Susamāhitasaṅkappā, sacittamanurakkhatha.

"Be heedful, mindful, and of good conduct, O monks. With well-collected resolve, protect your own mind."

‘‘Yo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye, appamatto vihassati;Pahāya jātisaṃsāraṃ, dukkhassantaṃ karissatī’’ti [viharissati (syā.), vihessati (sī.)].

"Whoever in this Dhamma-Vinaya dwells heedfully, having abandoned the round of births, will put an end to suffering."

## Tatiyo bhāṇavāro.

### The third recitation.

## Nāgāpalokitaṃ

### Elephant gaze.

186. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya vesāliṃ piṇḍāya pāvisi. Vesāliyaṃ piṇḍāya caritvā pacchābhattaṃ piṇḍapātappaṭikkanto nāgāpalokitaṃ vesāliṃ apaloketvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘idaṃ pacchimakaṃ, ānanda, tathāgatassa vesāliyā dassanaṃ bhavissati. Āyāmānanda, yena bhaṇḍagāmo [bhaṇḍugāmo (ka.)] tenupasaṅkamissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi.

186.Then, in the morning, the Blessed One, having dressed, took his bowl and robe, and entered Vesālī for alms. Having wandered for alms in Vesālī, after his meal and return from his alms round, after looking back at Vesālī with an elephant’s look, he addressed Venerable Ānanda: “Ānanda, this will be the Tathāgata’s last sight of Vesālī. Come, Ānanda, let us go to Bhaṇḍagāma.” “Yes, Bhante,” Venerable Ānanda replied to the Blessed One.

Atha kho bhagavā mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ yena bhaṇḍagāmo tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā bhaṇḍagāme viharati. Tatra kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘catunnaṃ, bhikkhave, dhammānaṃ ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamañceva tumhākañca. Katamesaṃ catunnaṃ? Ariyassa, bhikkhave, sīlassa ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamaṃ ceva tumhākañca. Ariyassa, bhikkhave, samādhissa ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamaṃ ceva tumhākañca. Ariyāya, bhikkhave, paññāya ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamaṃ ceva tumhākañca. Ariyāya, bhikkhave, vimuttiyā ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamaṃ ceva tumhākañca. Tayidaṃ, bhikkhave, ariyaṃ sīlaṃ anubuddhaṃ paṭividdhaṃ, ariyo samādhi anubuddho paṭividdho, ariyā paññā anubuddhā paṭividdhā, ariyā vimutti anubuddhā paṭividdhā, ucchinnā bhavataṇhā, khīṇā bhavanetti, natthi dāni punabbhavo’’ti. Idamavoca bhagavā, idaṃ vatvāna sugato athāparaṃ etadavoca satthā –

Then the Blessed One, together with a large company of bhikkhus, arrived at Bhaṇḍagāma. There the Blessed One stayed in Bhaṇḍagāma. There the Blessed One addressed the bhikkhus: “Bhikkhus, it is through not understanding, not penetrating four qualities that we have wandered and transmigrated for such a long time, both you and I. What four? It is through not understanding, not penetrating noble virtue that we have wandered and transmigrated for such a long time, both you and I. It is through not understanding, not penetrating noble samādhi that we have wandered and transmigrated for such a long time, both you and I. It is through not understanding, not penetrating noble wisdom that we have wandered and transmigrated for such a long time, both you and I. It is through not understanding, not penetrating noble liberation that we have wandered and transmigrated for such a long time, both you and I. But now, bhikkhus, noble virtue has been understood and penetrated, noble samādhi has been understood and penetrated, noble wisdom has been understood and penetrated, noble liberation has been understood and penetrated. Craving for being has been cut off, the guide to being has been destroyed, now there is no more renewed existence.” This is what the Blessed One said. Having said this, the Fortunate One, the Teacher, further said:

‘‘Sīlaṃ samādhi paññā ca, vimutti ca anuttarā;Anubuddhā ime dhammā, gotamena yasassinā.

“Virtue, samādhi, and wisdom, and unsurpassed liberation; These qualities were realized by the glorious Gotama.”

‘‘Iti buddho abhiññāya, dhammamakkhāsi bhikkhunaṃ;Dukkhassantakaro satthā, cakkhumā parinibbuto’’ti.

“Thus the Buddha, having directly known, declared the Dhamma to the bhikkhus; The Teacher, the ender of suffering, the One with Vision, is fully extinguished.”

Tatrāpi sudaṃ bhagavā bhaṇḍagāme viharanto etadeva bahulaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ dhammiṃ kathaṃ karoti – ‘‘iti sīlaṃ, iti samādhi, iti paññā. Sīlaparibhāvito samādhi mahapphalo hoti mahānisaṃso. Samādhiparibhāvitā paññā mahapphalā hoti mahānisaṃsā. Paññāparibhāvitaṃ cittaṃ sammadeva āsavehi vimuccati, seyyathidaṃ – kāmāsavā, bhavāsavā, avijjāsavā’’ti.

At that time also, while the Blessed One was staying at Bhaṇḍagāma, he often gave this Dhamma talk to the bhikkhus: “Such is virtue, such is samādhi, such is wisdom. samādhi, when imbued with virtue, is of great fruit and benefit. Wisdom, when imbued with samādhi, is of great fruit and benefit. The mind, when imbued with wisdom, is completely freed from the taints—namely, the taint of sensual desire, the taint of existence, and the taint of ignorance.”

## Catumahāpadesakathā

### The Account of the Four Great Authorities

187. Atha kho bhagavā bhaṇḍagāme yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘āyāmānanda, yena hatthigāmo, yena ambagāmo, yena jambugāmo, yena bhoganagaraṃ tenupasaṅkamissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi. Atha kho bhagavā mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ yena bhoganagaraṃ tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā bhoganagare viharati ānande [sānandare (ka.)] cetiye. Tatra kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘cattārome, bhikkhave, mahāpadese desessāmi, taṃ suṇātha, sādhukaṃ manasikarotha, bhāsissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho te bhikkhū bhagavato paccassosuṃ. Bhagavā etadavoca –

187.Then, after staying at Bhaṇḍagāma as long as he pleased, the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: “Come, Ānanda, let us go to Hatthigāma, to Ambagāma, to Jambugāma, and then to Bhoganagara.” “Yes, Bhante,” Venerable Ānanda replied to the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One, together with a large Saṅgha of bhikkhus, arrived at Bhoganagara. There, the Blessed One stayed at the Ānanda Shrine in Bhoganagara. There, the Blessed One addressed the bhikkhus: “Bhikkhus, I will teach you the four great authorities. Listen carefully and pay close attention, I will speak.” “Yes, Bhante,” those bhikkhus replied to the Blessed One. The Blessed One said:

188. ‘‘Idha, bhikkhave, bhikkhu evaṃ vadeyya – ‘sammukhā metaṃ, āvuso, bhagavato sutaṃ sammukhā paṭiggahitaṃ, ayaṃ dhammo ayaṃ vinayo idaṃ satthusāsana’nti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno bhāsitaṃ neva abhinanditabbaṃ nappaṭikkositabbaṃ. Anabhinanditvā appaṭikkositvā tāni padabyañjanāni sādhukaṃ uggahetvā sutte osāretabbāni [otāretabbāni], vinaye sandassetabbāni. Tāni ce sutte osāriyamānāni [otāriyamānāni] vinaye sandassiyamānāni na ceva sutte osaranti [otaranti (sī. pī. a. ni. 4.180], na ca vinaye sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ na ceva tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; imassa ca bhikkhuno duggahita’nti. Itihetaṃ, bhikkhave, chaḍḍeyyātha. Tāni ce sutte osāriyamānāni vinaye sandassiyamānāni sutte ceva osaranti, vinaye ca sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; imassa ca bhikkhuno suggahita’nti. Idaṃ, bhikkhave, paṭhamaṃ mahāpadesaṃ dhāreyyātha.

188.“Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu might say: ‘Friend, I heard this in the presence of the Blessed One, I received it in the presence of the Blessed One: This is the Dhamma, this is the Vinaya, this is the Teacher’s instruction.’ Bhikkhus, you should neither approve nor reject that bhikkhu’s statement. Without approving or rejecting it, you should carefully learn those words and phrases and then compare them with the Suttas and review them in the Vinaya. If, when compared with the Suttas and reviewed in the Vinaya, they neither accord with the Suttas nor appear in the Vinaya, you should conclude: ‘Surely, this is not the word of the Blessed One; this bhikkhu has misunderstood it.’ Thus, bhikkhus, you should discard it. But if, when compared with the Suttas and reviewed in the Vinaya, they accord with the Suttas and appear in the Vinaya, you should conclude: ‘Surely, this is the word of the Blessed One; this bhikkhu has understood it well.’ Bhikkhus, this is the first great authority you should bear in mind.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu evaṃ vadeyya – ‘amukasmiṃ nāma āvāse saṅgho viharati sathero sapāmokkho. Tassa me saṅghassa sammukhā sutaṃ sammukhā paṭiggahitaṃ, ayaṃ dhammo ayaṃ vinayo idaṃ satthusāsana’nti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno bhāsitaṃ neva abhinanditabbaṃ nappaṭikkositabbaṃ. Anabhinanditvā appaṭikkositvā tāni padabyañjanāni sādhukaṃ uggahetvā sutte osāretabbāni, vinaye sandassetabbāni. Tāni ce sutte osāriyamānāni vinaye sandassiyamānāni na ceva sutte osaranti, na ca vinaye sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ na ceva tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; tassa ca saṅghassa duggahita’nti. Itihetaṃ, bhikkhave, chaḍḍeyyātha. Tāni ce sutte osāriyamānāni vinaye sandassiyamānāni sutte ceva osaranti vinaye ca sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; tassa ca saṅghassa suggahita’nti. Idaṃ, bhikkhave, dutiyaṃ mahāpadesaṃ dhāreyyātha.

“Here, bhikkhus, suppose a bhikkhu were to say: ‘In such and such a monastery the Saṅgha resides, with elders and leaders. I’ve heard and received this in the presence of that Saṅgha: this is the Dhamma, this is the Vinaya, this is the Teacher’s instruction.’ You should neither approve nor reject that bhikkhu’s words. Without approving or rejecting them, you should carefully learn those words and phrases, then compare them with the Suttas and review them in the Vinaya. If, when compared with the Suttas and reviewed in the Vinaya, they neither accord with the Suttas nor appear in the Vinaya, you should conclude: ‘Surely, this is not the word of the Blessed One, and has been wrongly grasped by that Saṅgha.’ In that case, bhikkhus, you should reject it. But if, when compared with the Suttas and reviewed in the Vinaya, they accord with the Suttas and appear in the Vinaya, you should conclude: ‘Surely, this is the word of the Blessed One, and has been rightly grasped by that Saṅgha.’ This, bhikkhus, is the second great authority you should bear in mind.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu evaṃ vadeyya – ‘amukasmiṃ nāma āvāse sambahulā therā bhikkhū viharanti bahussutā āgatāgamā dhammadharā vinayadharā mātikādharā. Tesaṃ me therānaṃ sammukhā sutaṃ sammukhā paṭiggahitaṃ – ayaṃ dhammo ayaṃ vinayo idaṃ satthusāsana’nti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno bhāsitaṃ neva abhinanditabbaṃ…pe… na ca vinaye sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ na ceva tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; tesañca therānaṃ duggahita’nti. Itihetaṃ, bhikkhave, chaḍḍeyyātha. Tāni ce sutte osāriyamānāni…pe… vinaye ca sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; tesañca therānaṃ suggahita’nti. Idaṃ, bhikkhave, tatiyaṃ mahāpadesaṃ dhāreyyātha.

“Here, bhikkhus, suppose a bhikkhu were to say: ‘In such and such a monastery, many elder bhikkhus dwell who are learned, versed in the traditions, upholders of the Dhamma, upholders of the Vinaya, upholders of the Mātikā. I have heard and received this directly from those elders: this is the Dhamma, this is the Vinaya, this is the Teacher’s instruction.’ His statement, bhikkhus, should neither be approved nor rejected… If, when compared with the Suttas and reviewed in the Vinaya, they neither accord with the Suttas nor appear in the Vinaya, you should conclude: ‘Surely, this is not the word of the Blessed One; it has been wrongly grasped by those elders.’ Thus, bhikkhus, you should reject it. But if, when compared with the Suttas and reviewed in the Vinaya, they accord with the Suttas and appear in the Vinaya, you should conclude: ‘Surely, this is the word of the Blessed One; it has been correctly grasped by those elders.’ This, bhikkhus, is the third great authority you should bear in mind.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu evaṃ vadeyya – ‘amukasmiṃ nāma āvāse eko thero bhikkhu viharati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo. Tassa me therassa sammukhā sutaṃ sammukhā paṭiggahitaṃ – ayaṃ dhammo ayaṃ vinayo idaṃ satthusāsana’nti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno bhāsitaṃ neva abhinanditabbaṃ nappaṭikkositabbaṃ. Anabhinanditvā appaṭikkositvā tāni padabyañjanāni sādhukaṃ uggahetvā sutte osāritabbāni, vinaye sandassetabbāni. Tāni ce sutte osāriyamānāni vinaye sandassiyamānāni na ceva sutte osaranti, na ca vinaye sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ na ceva tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; tassa ca therassa duggahita’nti. Itihetaṃ, bhikkhave, chaḍḍeyyātha. Tāni ca sutte osāriyamānāni vinaye sandassiyamānāni sutte ceva osaranti, vinaye ca sandissanti, niṭṭhamettha gantabbaṃ – ‘addhā, idaṃ tassa bhagavato vacanaṃ; tassa ca therassa suggahita’nti. Idaṃ, bhikkhave, catutthaṃ mahāpadesaṃ dhāreyyātha. Ime kho, bhikkhave, cattāro mahāpadese dhāreyyāthā’’ti.

“Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu might speak thus: ‘In such and such a dwelling place there dwells an elder bhikkhu who is learned, who has mastered the traditions, a Dhamma-bearer, a Vinaya-bearer, a Mātikā-bearer. I have heard this in the presence of that elder, I have received this in his presence: “This is the Dhamma, this is the Vinaya, this is the Teacher’s instruction.”’ Bhikkhus, that bhikkhu’s statement should neither be approved nor rejected. Without approving or rejecting it, those words and phrases should be carefully learned, then checked against the Suttas and compared with the Vinaya. If, when checked against the Suttas and compared with the Vinaya, they do not fit the Suttas or accord with the Vinaya, then this conclusion should be reached: ‘Certainly, this is not the word of the Blessed One; it has been wrongly grasped by that elder.’ Thus, bhikkhus, you should discard it. But if, when checked against the Suttas and compared with the Vinaya, they fit the Suttas and accord with the Vinaya, then this conclusion should be reached: ‘Certainly, this is the word of the Blessed One; it has been correctly grasped by that elder.’ Bhikkhus, this is the fourth great authority you should bear in mind. Bhikkhus, you should bear in mind these four great authorities.”

Tatrapi sudaṃ bhagavā bhoganagare viharanto ānande cetiye etadeva bahulaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ dhammiṃ kathaṃ karoti – ‘‘iti sīlaṃ, iti samādhi, iti paññā. Sīlaparibhāvito samādhi mahapphalo hoti mahānisaṃso. Samādhiparibhāvitā paññā mahapphalā hoti mahānisaṃsā. Paññāparibhāvitaṃ cittaṃ sammadeva āsavehi vimuccati, seyyathidaṃ – kāmāsavā, bhavāsavā, avijjāsavā’’ti.

There, too, while the Blessed One was dwelling at Bhoganagara, at the Ānanda Shrine, he often gave this Dhamma talk to the bhikkhus: “Such is virtue, such is samādhi, such is wisdom. samādhi, when developed by virtue, is of great fruit and great benefit. Wisdom, when developed by samādhi, is of great fruit and great benefit. The mind, when developed by wisdom, is completely liberated from the taints, that is, from the taint of sensual desire, the taint of existence, and the taint of ignorance.”

## Kammāraputtacundavatthu

### The Story of Cunda, the Smith’s Son

189. Atha kho bhagavā bhoganagare yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘āyāmānanda, yena pāvā tenupasaṅkamissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi. Atha kho bhagavā mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ yena pāvā tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā pāvāyaṃ viharati cundassa kammāraputtassa ambavane. Assosi kho cundo kammāraputto – ‘‘bhagavā kira pāvaṃ anuppatto, pāvāyaṃ viharati mayhaṃ ambavane’’ti. Atha kho cundo kammāraputto yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho cundaṃ kammāraputtaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho cundo kammāraputto bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho cundo kammāraputto bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

189.Then, having stayed at Bhoganagara as long as he pleased, the Blessed One addressed the Venerable Ānanda: “Come, Ānanda, let us go to Pāvā.” “Yes, Venerable sir,” the Venerable Ānanda replied to the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One, together with a large community of bhikkhus, arrived at Pāvā. There, at Pāvā, the Blessed One dwelt in Cunda the smith’s son’s mango grove. Cunda the smith’s son heard: ‘The Blessed One, it seems, has arrived at Pāvā and is dwelling at Pāvā in my mango grove.’ Then Cunda the smith’s son approached the Blessed One; having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. The Blessed One instructed, urged, enlightened, and gladdened Cunda the smith’s son with a Dhamma talk. Then Cunda the smith’s son, having been instructed, urged, enlightened, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, may the Blessed One consent to accept tomorrow’s meal from me, together with the community of bhikkhus.” The Blessed One consented by silence. Then Cunda the smith’s son, knowing of the Blessed One’s consent, rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed.

Atha kho cundo kammāraputto tassā rattiyā accayena sake nivesane paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā pahūtañca sūkaramaddavaṃ bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena yena cundassa kammāraputtassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi. Nisajja kho bhagavā cundaṃ kammāraputtaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘yaṃ te, cunda, sūkaramaddavaṃ paṭiyattaṃ, tena maṃ parivisa. Yaṃ panaññaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyattaṃ, tena bhikkhusaṅghaṃ parivisā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho cundo kammāraputto bhagavato paṭissutvā yaṃ ahosi sūkaramaddavaṃ paṭiyattaṃ, tena bhagavantaṃ parivisi. Yaṃ panaññaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyattaṃ, tena bhikkhusaṅghaṃ parivisi. Atha kho bhagavā cundaṃ kammāraputtaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘yaṃ te, cunda, sūkaramaddavaṃ avasiṭṭhaṃ, taṃ sobbhe nikhaṇāhi. Nāhaṃ taṃ, cunda, passāmi sadevake loke samārake sabrahmake sassamaṇabrāhmaṇiyā pajāya sadevamanussāya, yassa taṃ paribhuttaṃ sammā pariṇāmaṃ gaccheyya aññatra tathāgatassā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho cundo kammāraputto bhagavato paṭissutvā yaṃ ahosi sūkaramaddavaṃ avasiṭṭhaṃ, taṃ sobbhe nikhaṇitvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho cundaṃ kammāraputtaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

Then, when that night had passed, Cunda the smith’s son had choice hard and soft foods prepared in his own home, together with a large quantity of tender pork. He announced the time to the Blessed One: “It is time, Venerable sir, the meal is ready.” Then, in the forenoon, having dressed and taken his bowl and outer robe, the Blessed One went with the community of bhikkhus to the home of Cunda the smith’s son. Having arrived, he sat down on the seat prepared for him. Having sat down, the Blessed One addressed Cunda the smith’s son: “Cunda, serve me with the tender pork you have prepared. Serve the community of bhikkhus with the other hard and soft foods you have prepared.” “Yes, Venerable sir,” replied Cunda the smith’s son, and he served the Blessed One with the tender pork he had prepared, and the community of bhikkhus with the other hard and soft foods he had prepared. Then the Blessed One addressed Cunda the smith’s son: “Cunda, bury whatever remains of the tender pork in a pit. For I do not see anyone in this world with its devas, Māras, and Brahmās, among this generation with its recluses and brahmins, its devas and humans, who could properly digest it except for the Tathāgata.” “Yes, Venerable sir,” replied Cunda the smith’s son, and he buried the remaining tender pork in a pit. Then he approached the Blessed One; having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. While Cunda the smith’s son was sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, urged, enlightened, and gladdened him with a Dhamma talk. Then, rising from his seat, he departed.

190. Atha kho bhagavato cundassa kammāraputtassa bhattaṃ bhuttāvissa kharo ābādho uppajji, lohitapakkhandikā pabāḷhā vedanā vattanti māraṇantikā. Tā sudaṃ bhagavā sato sampajāno adhivāsesi avihaññamāno. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘āyāmānanda, yena kusinārā tenupasaṅkamissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi.

190.Then, after the Blessed One had eaten the meal provided by Cunda the smith’s son, a severe illness arose in him, a bloody dysentery, with sharp, deadly pains. But the Blessed One endured it, mindful and clearly comprehending, without being overwhelmed. Then the Blessed One addressed the Venerable Ānanda: “Come, Ānanda, let us go to Kusinārā.” “Yes, Venerable sir,” the Venerable Ānanda replied to the Blessed One.

Cundassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā, kammārassāti me sutaṃ;Ābādhaṃ samphusī dhīro, pabāḷhaṃ māraṇantikaṃ.

Having eaten Cunda the smith’s meal, so I have heard, the wise one was afflicted by an illness, severe, leading to death.

Bhuttassa ca sūkaramaddavena,Byādhippabāḷho udapādi satthuno;Virecamāno [viriccamāno (sī. syā. ka.), viriñcamāno (?)] bhagavā avoca,Gacchāmahaṃ kusināraṃ nagaranti.

Having eaten the tender pork, a severe illness arose in the Teacher. While purging, the Blessed One said: ‘I shall go to the city of Kusinārā.’

## Pānīyāharaṇaṃ

### Fetching water.

191. Atha kho bhagavā maggā okkamma yena aññataraṃ rukkhamūlaṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, ānanda, catugguṇaṃ saṅghāṭiṃ paññapehi, kilantosmi, ānanda, nisīdissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paṭissutvā catugguṇaṃ saṅghāṭiṃ paññapesi. Nisīdi bhagavā paññatte āsane. Nisajja kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, ānanda, pānīyaṃ āhara, pipāsitosmi, ānanda, pivissāmī’’ti. Evaṃ vutte āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idāni, bhante, pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni atikkantāni, taṃ cakkacchinnaṃ udakaṃ parittaṃ luḷitaṃ āvilaṃ sandati. Ayaṃ, bhante, kakudhā [kakuthā (sī. pī.)] nadī avidūre acchodakā sātodakā sītodakā setodakā [setakā (sī.)] suppatitthā ramaṇīyā. Ettha bhagavā pānīyañca pivissati, gattāni ca sītī [sītaṃ (sī. pī. ka.)] karissatī’’ti.

191.Then the Blessed One stepped off the road and went to the foot of a certain tree. Having approached, he addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Come, Ānanda, fold my outer robe into four and spread it out for me. I am tired, Ānanda, I will sit down." "Yes, Venerable Sir," replied Venerable Ānanda, and he folded the outer robe into four and spread it out. The Blessed One sat down on the prepared seat. Having sat down, the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Come, Ānanda, fetch me some water. I am thirsty, Ānanda, I will drink." When this was said, Venerable Ānanda replied to the Blessed One: "Just now, Venerable Sir, about five hundred carts have passed by. The water churned by their wheels is little, agitated, muddy, and flowing. Not far from here, Venerable Sir, is the Kakudhā River with clear water, agreeable water, cool water, pure water, with good landing places, delightful. There the Blessed One can drink water and cool his limbs."

Dutiyampi kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, ānanda, pānīyaṃ āhara, pipāsitosmi, ānanda, pivissāmī’’ti. Dutiyampi kho āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idāni, bhante, pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni atikkantāni, taṃ cakkacchinnaṃ udakaṃ parittaṃ luḷitaṃ āvilaṃ sandati. Ayaṃ, bhante, kakudhā nadī avidūre acchodakā sātodakā sītodakā setodakā suppatitthā ramaṇīyā. Ettha bhagavā pānīyañca pivissati, gattāni ca sītīkarissatī’’ti.

A second time, the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Come, Ānanda, fetch me some water. I am thirsty, Ānanda, I will drink." A second time, Venerable Ānanda said to the Blessed One: "Just now, Venerable Sir, about five hundred carts have passed by. That water, churned by their wheels, is little, agitated, muddy, and flowing. But, Venerable Sir, the Kakudhā River is not far from here, with clear water, agreeable water, cool water, pure water, with good landing places, delightful. There the Blessed One can drink water and cool his limbs."

Tatiyampi kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, ānanda, pānīyaṃ āhara, pipāsitosmi, ānanda, pivissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paṭissutvā pattaṃ gahetvā yena sā nadikā tenupasaṅkami. Atha kho sā nadikā cakkacchinnā parittā luḷitā āvilā sandamānā, āyasmante ānande upasaṅkamante acchā vippasannā anāvilā sandittha [sandati (syā.)]. Atha kho āyasmato ānandassa etadahosi – ‘‘acchariyaṃ vata, bho, abbhutaṃ vata, bho, tathāgatassa mahiddhikatā mahānubhāvatā. Ayañhi sā nadikā cakkacchinnā parittā luḷitā āvilā sandamānā mayi upasaṅkamante acchā vippasannā anāvilā sandatī’’ti. Pattena pānīyaṃ ādāya yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘acchariyaṃ, bhante, abbhutaṃ, bhante, tathāgatassa mahiddhikatā mahānubhāvatā. Idāni sā bhante nadikā cakkacchinnā parittā luḷitā āvilā sandamānā mayi upasaṅkamante acchā vippasannā anāvilā sandittha. Pivatu bhagavā pānīyaṃ pivatu sugato pānīya’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pānīyaṃ apāyi.

A third time, the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Come, Ānanda, fetch me some water. I am thirsty, Ānanda, I will drink." "Yes, Venerable Sir," replied Venerable Ānanda, and taking a bowl, he went to the river. Now, that river, which had been churned by wheels, little, agitated, muddy, and flowing, as Venerable Ānanda approached, became clear, limpid, and undisturbed. Then it occurred to Venerable Ānanda: "How wonderful, how marvelous is the great power and might of the Tathāgata! For this river, which was churned by wheels, little, agitated, muddy, and flowing, as I approached, became clear, limpid, and undisturbed." Taking water in the bowl, he returned to the Blessed One and said: "How wonderful, Venerable Sir, how marvelous is the great power and might of the Tathāgata! Just now, Venerable Sir, this river, which was churned by wheels, little, agitated, muddy, and flowing, as I approached, became clear, limpid, and undisturbed. Let the Blessed One drink the water, let the Sugata drink the water." Then the Blessed One drank the water.

## Pukkusamallaputtavatthu

### The Story of Pukkusa, Son of a Malla

192. Tena rokho pana samayena pukkuso mallaputto āḷārassa kālāmassa sāvako kusinārāya pāvaṃ addhānamaggappaṭippanno hoti. Addasā kho pukkuso mallaputto bhagavantaṃ aññatarasmiṃ rukkhamūle nisinnaṃ. Disvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho pukkuso mallaputto bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘acchariyaṃ, bhante, abbhutaṃ, bhante, santena vata, bhante, pabbajitā vihārena viharanti. Bhūtapubbaṃ, bhante, āḷāro kālāmo addhānamaggappaṭippanno maggā okkamma avidūre aññatarasmiṃ rukkhamūle divāvihāraṃ nisīdi. Atha kho, bhante, pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni āḷāraṃ kālāmaṃ nissāya nissāya atikkamiṃsu. Atha kho, bhante, aññataro puriso tassa sakaṭasatthassa [sakaṭasatassa (ka.)] piṭṭhito piṭṭhito āgacchanto yena āḷāro kālāmo tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā āḷāraṃ kālāmaṃ etadavoca – ‘api, bhante, pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni atikkantāni addasā’ti? ‘Na kho ahaṃ, āvuso, addasa’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, saddaṃ assosī’ti? ‘Na kho ahaṃ, āvuso, saddaṃ assosi’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, sutto ahosī’ti? ‘Na kho ahaṃ, āvuso, sutto ahosi’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, saññī ahosī’ti? ‘Evamāvuso’ti. ‘So tvaṃ, bhante, saññī samāno jāgaro pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni nissāya nissāya atikkantāni neva addasa, na pana saddaṃ assosi; apisu [api hi (sī. syā. pī.)] te, bhante, saṅghāṭi rajena okiṇṇā’ti? ‘Evamāvuso’ti. Atha kho, bhante, tassa purisassa etadahosi – ‘acchariyaṃ vata bho, abbhutaṃ vata bho, santena vata bho pabbajitā vihārena viharanti. Yatra hi nāma saññī samāno jāgaro pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni nissāya nissāya atikkantāni neva dakkhati, na pana saddaṃ sossatī’ti! Āḷāre kālāme uḷāraṃ pasādaṃ pavedetvā pakkāmī’’ti.

192.At that time, Pukkusa the Mallan, a disciple of Āḷāra Kālāma, was traveling along the road from Kusinārā to Pāvā. Pukkusa the Mallan saw the Blessed One seated at the root of a tree. Having seen him, he approached the Blessed One, paid homage, and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, Pukkusa the Mallan said to the Blessed One: "Wonderful, venerable sir! Astonishing, venerable sir! How peaceful, indeed, venerable sir, is the dwelling of those gone forth! Once, venerable sir, Āḷāra Kālāma was traveling along a road. He stepped off the road and sat down at the root of a tree for his midday rest. Then, venerable sir, about five hundred carts passed by close to Āḷāra Kālāma. Then, venerable sir, a certain man following behind those carts approached Āḷāra Kālāma and said: ‘Did you see, venerable sir, about five hundred carts pass by?’ ‘No, friend, I did not see them.’ ‘But, venerable sir, did you hear the sound?’ ‘No, friend, I did not hear the sound.’ ‘Then, venerable sir, were you asleep?’ ‘No, friend, I was not asleep.’ ‘Then, venerable sir, were you conscious?’ ‘Yes, friend.’ ‘So, venerable sir, being conscious and awake, five hundred carts passed close by, yet you neither saw them nor heard the sound? And yet, venerable sir, your outer robe is covered with dust!’ ‘Yes, friend.’ Then, venerable sir, that man thought: ‘Wonderful indeed, sir! Astonishing indeed, sir! How peaceful indeed is the dwelling of those gone forth, who, being conscious and awake, do not see or hear the sound of five hundred carts passing close by!’ Having declared his supreme confidence in Āḷāra Kālāma, he departed."

193. ‘‘Taṃ kiṃ maññasi, pukkusa, katamaṃ nu kho dukkarataraṃ vā durabhisambhavataraṃ vā – yo vā saññī samāno jāgaro pañcamattāni sakaṭasatāni nissāya nissāya atikkantāni neva passeyya, na pana saddaṃ suṇeyya; yo vā saññī samāno jāgaro deve vassante deve gaḷagaḷāyante vijjullatāsu [vijjutāsu (sī. syā. pī.)] niccharantīsu asaniyā phalantiyā neva passeyya, na pana saddaṃ suṇeyyā’’ti? ‘‘Kiñhi, bhante, karissanti pañca vā sakaṭasatāni cha vā sakaṭasatāni satta vā sakaṭasatāni aṭṭha vā sakaṭasatāni nava vā sakaṭasatāni [nava vā sakaṭasatāni dasa vā sakaṭasatāni (sī.)], sakaṭasahassaṃ vā sakaṭasatasahassaṃ vā. Atha kho etadeva dukkarataraṃ ceva durabhisambhavatarañca yo saññī samāno jāgaro deve vassante deve gaḷagaḷāyante vijjullatāsu niccharantīsu asaniyā phalantiyā neva passeyya, na pana saddaṃ suṇeyyā’’ti.

193."What do you think, Pukkusa, which is more difficult and harder to achieve—someone who is conscious and awake not seeing or hearing five hundred carts passing by one after another, or someone who is conscious and awake not seeing or hearing when it is raining, when thunder is rumbling, when lightning is darting, and when thunderbolts are cracking?" "What, venerable sir, would five hundred carts matter, or six hundred, seven hundred, eight hundred, nine hundred, or a thousand carts, or even a hundred thousand carts? But indeed, it is more difficult and harder to achieve for someone who is conscious and awake not to see or hear when it is raining, when thunder is rumbling, when lightning is darting, and when thunderbolts are cracking."

‘‘Ekamidāhaṃ, pukkusa, samayaṃ ātumāyaṃ viharāmi bhusāgāre. Tena kho pana samayena deve vassante deve gaḷagaḷāyante vijjullatāsu niccharantīsu asaniyā phalantiyā avidūre bhusāgārassa dve kassakā bhātaro hatā cattāro ca balibaddā [balibaddā (sī. pī.)]. Atha kho, pukkusa, ātumāya mahājanakāyo nikkhamitvā yena te dve kassakā bhātaro hatā cattāro ca balibaddā tenupasaṅkami. Tena kho panāhaṃ, pukkusa, samayena bhusāgārā nikkhamitvā bhusāgāradvāre abbhokāse caṅkamāmi. Atha kho, pukkusa, aññataro puriso tamhā mahājanakāyā yenāhaṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā maṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhitaṃ kho ahaṃ, pukkusa, taṃ purisaṃ etadavocaṃ – ‘kiṃ nu kho eso, āvuso, mahājanakāyo sannipatito’ti? ‘Idāni, bhante, deve vassante deve gaḷagaḷāyante vijjullatāsu niccharantīsu asaniyā phalantiyā dve kassakā bhātaro hatā cattāro ca balibaddā. Ettheso mahājanakāyo sannipatito. Tvaṃ pana, bhante, kva ahosī’ti? ‘Idheva kho ahaṃ, āvuso, ahosi’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, addasā’ti? ‘Na kho ahaṃ, āvuso, addasa’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, saddaṃ assosī’ti? ‘Na kho ahaṃ, āvuso, saddaṃ assosi’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, sutto ahosī’ti? ‘Na kho ahaṃ, āvuso, sutto ahosi’nti. ‘Kiṃ pana, bhante, saññī ahosī’ti? ‘Evamāvuso’ti. ‘So tvaṃ, bhante, saññī samāno jāgaro deve vassante deve gaḷagaḷāyante vijjullatāsu niccharantīsu asaniyā phalantiyā neva addasa, na pana saddaṃ assosī’ti? ‘‘Evamāvuso’’ti?

"Once, Pukkusa, I was staying in Ātumā in a threshing shed. At that time, it was raining, the gods were roaring, lightning was darting, and thunderbolts were crashing. Not far from the threshing shed, two farmer brothers were killed, along with four oxen. Then, Pukkusa, a large crowd of people came out from Ātumā and approached the place where those two farmer brothers and the four oxen had been killed. At that time, Pukkusa, I had come out of the threshing shed and was walking back and forth in the open space at the door of the threshing shed. Then, Pukkusa, a certain man from that large crowd approached me. Having approached, he paid homage to me and stood to one side. Standing to one side, Pukkusa, I said to that man: ‘Why, friend, has this large crowd gathered?’ ‘Just now, venerable sir, while it was raining, the gods were roaring, lightning was darting, and thunderbolts crashing, two farmer brothers were killed, along with four oxen. That is why this large crowd has gathered. But where were you, venerable sir?’ ‘I was right here, friend.’ ‘But, venerable sir, did you see it?’ ‘No, friend, I did not see it.’ ‘But, venerable sir, did you hear the sound?’ ‘No, friend, I did not hear the sound.’ ‘But, venerable sir, were you asleep?’ ‘No, friend, I was not asleep.’ ‘But, venerable sir, were you conscious?’ ‘Yes, friend.’ ‘So, venerable sir, being conscious and awake, while it was raining, the gods were roaring, lightning was darting, and thunderbolts crashing, you neither saw nor heard the sound?’ ‘Yes, friend.’"

‘‘Atha kho, pukkusa, purisassa etadahosi – ‘acchariyaṃ vata bho, abbhutaṃ vata bho, santena vata bho pabbajitā vihārena viharanti. Yatra hi nāma saññī samāno jāgaro deve vassante deve gaḷagaḷāyante vijjullatāsu niccharantīsu asaniyā phalantiyā neva dakkhati, na pana saddaṃ sossatī’ti [suṇissati (syā.)]. Mayi uḷāraṃ pasādaṃ pavedetvā maṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmī’’ti.

"Then, Pukkusa, that man had this thought: ‘How wonderful, how amazing! How peacefully indeed do those gone forth live! For although conscious and awake, he neither saw nor heard the sound when it was raining, when thunder was rumbling, when lightning was darting, and when thunderbolts were crashing.’ Having expressed supreme confidence in me, he paid homage, circumambulated me, and departed."

Evaṃ vutte pukkuso mallaputto bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘esāhaṃ, bhante, yo me āḷāre kālāme pasādo taṃ mahāvāte vā ophuṇāmi sīghasotāya [siṅghasotāya (ka.)] vā nadiyā pavāhemi. Abhikkantaṃ, bhante, abhikkantaṃ, bhante! Seyyathāpi, bhante, nikkujjitaṃ vā ukkujjeyya, paṭicchannaṃ vā vivareyya, mūḷhassa vā maggaṃ ācikkheyya, andhakāre vā telapajjotaṃ dhāreyya ‘cakkhumanto rūpāni dakkhantī’ti; evamevaṃ bhagavatā anekapariyāyena dhammo pakāsito. Esāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi dhammañca bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇaṃ gata’’nti.

When this was said, Pukkusa the Mallan said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, the confidence I had in Āḷāra Kālāma, that I scatter to a great wind or let flow away in a swift-flowing river. Magnificent, venerable sir! Magnificent, venerable sir! Just as, venerable sir, one might set upright what was overturned, reveal what was hidden, show the way to one who is lost, or hold up a lamp in the darkness so that those with eyes might see forms—just so has the Dhamma been made clear by the Blessed One in many ways. I go to the Blessed One for refuge, to the Dhamma, and to the Sangha of bhikkhus. May the Blessed One remember me as a lay follower who has gone for refuge from this day forth as long as life lasts."

194. Atha kho pukkuso mallaputto aññataraṃ purisaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, bhaṇe, siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ dhāraṇīyaṃ āharā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho so puriso pukkusassa mallaputtassa paṭissutvā taṃ siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ dhāraṇīyaṃ āhari [āharasi (ka.)]. Atha kho pukkuso mallaputto taṃ siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ dhāraṇīyaṃ bhagavato upanāmesi – ‘‘idaṃ, bhante, siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ dhāraṇīyaṃ, taṃ me bhagavā paṭiggaṇhātu anukampaṃ upādāyā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, pukkusa, ekena maṃ acchādehi, ekena ānanda’’nti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho pukkuso mallaputto bhagavato paṭissutvā ekena bhagavantaṃ acchādeti, ekena āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ. Atha kho bhagavā pukkusaṃ mallaputtaṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho pukkuso mallaputto bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

194.Then Pukkusa the Mallan addressed a certain man, saying, "Come now, friend, bring me a pair of burnished-gold robes, to be worn." "Yes, venerable sir," replied that man, and having assented to Pukkusa the Mallan, he brought that pair of burnished-gold robes, to be worn. Then Pukkusa the Mallan offered that pair of burnished-gold robes, to be worn, to the Blessed One, saying, "Venerable sir, here is this pair of burnished-gold robes, to be worn. May the Blessed One accept it out of compassion for me." "Well then, Pukkusa, clothe me with one, and Ānanda with the other." "Yes, venerable sir," replied Pukkusa the Mallan, and having assented to the Blessed One, he clothed the Blessed One with one, and Venerable Ānanda with the other. Then the Blessed One instructed, aroused, inspired, and gladdened Pukkusa the Mallan with a Dhamma talk. Then, having been instructed, aroused, inspired, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, Pukkusa the Mallan rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed.

195. Atha kho āyasmā ānando acirapakkante pukkuse mallaputte taṃ siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ dhāraṇīyaṃ bhagavato kāyaṃ upanāmesi. Taṃ bhagavato kāyaṃ upanāmitaṃ hataccikaṃ viya [vītaccikaṃviya (sī. pī.)] khāyati. Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘acchariyaṃ, bhante, abbhutaṃ, bhante, yāva parisuddho, bhante, tathāgatassa chavivaṇṇo pariyodāto. Idaṃ, bhante, siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ dhāraṇīyaṃ bhagavato kāyaṃ upanāmitaṃ hataccikaṃ viya khāyatī’’ti. ‘‘Evametaṃ, ānanda, evametaṃ, ānanda dvīsu kālesu ativiya tathāgatassa kāyo parisuddho hoti chavivaṇṇo pariyodāto. Katamesu dvīsu? Yañca, ānanda, rattiṃ tathāgato anuttaraṃ sammāsambodhiṃ abhisambujjhati, yañca rattiṃ anupādisesāya nibbānadhātuyā parinibbāyati. Imesu kho, ānanda, dvīsu kālesu ativiya tathāgatassa kāyo parisuddho hoti chavivaṇṇo pariyodāto. ‘‘Ajja kho, panānanda, rattiyā pacchime yāme kusinārāyaṃ upavattane mallānaṃ sālavane antarena [antare (syā.)] yamakasālānaṃ tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati [bhavissatīti (ka.)]. Āyāmānanda, yena kakudhā nadī tenupasaṅkamissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi.

195.Then, not long after Pukkusa the Mallan had left, Venerable Ānanda applied that pair of burnished-gold robes, to be worn, to the Blessed One's body. When applied to the Blessed One's body, it appeared as if it had lost its luster. Then Venerable Ānanda said to the Blessed One, "It is wonderful, venerable sir, it is marvelous, venerable sir, how exceedingly pure and bright the Tathāgata's complexion is. Venerable sir, when this pair of burnished-gold robes, to be worn, is applied to the Blessed One's body, it appears as if it had lost its luster." "It is so, Ānanda, it is so, Ānanda. There are two occasions, Ānanda, when the Tathāgata's body is exceedingly pure and bright. What are the two? The night when the Tathāgata awakens to unsurpassed perfect enlightenment, and the night when the Tathāgata attains final Nibbāna without any remainder of clinging. On these two occasions, Ānanda, the Tathāgata's body is exceedingly pure and bright. And today, Ānanda, in the last watch of the night, the Tathāgata's Parinibbāna will take place in the sal grove of the Mallas at Kusinārā, between the twin sal trees. Come, Ānanda, let us go to the Kakutthā River." "Yes, venerable sir," replied Venerable Ānanda to the Blessed One.

Siṅgīvaṇṇaṃ yugamaṭṭhaṃ, pukkuso abhihārayi;Tena acchādito satthā, hemavaṇṇo asobhathāti.

The pair of burnished-gold robes, Pukkusa offered; Clothed with them, the Teacher shone, golden in hue.

196. Atha kho bhagavā mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ yena kakudhā nadī tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā kakudhaṃ nadiṃ ajjhogāhetvā nhatvā ca pivitvā ca paccuttaritvā yena ambavanaṃ tenupasaṅkami. Upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ cundakaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, cundaka, catugguṇaṃ saṅghāṭiṃ paññapehi, kilantosmi, cundaka, nipajjissāmī’’ti.

196.Then the Blessed One, together with a large community of bhikkhus, went to the Kakudhā River. Having approached the Kakudhā River, he plunged into the Kakudhā River, bathed, drank, and came back out. Then he went to the mango grove. Having approached, he addressed Venerable Cundaka, saying, "Come, Cundaka, fold the outer robe into four, prepare it for me. I am tired, Cundaka, I will lie down."

‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā cundako bhagavato paṭissutvā catugguṇaṃ saṅghāṭiṃ paññapesi. Atha kho bhagavā dakkhiṇena passena sīhaseyyaṃ kappesi pāde pādaṃ accādhāya sato sampajāno uṭṭhānasaññaṃ manasikaritvā. Āyasmā pana cundako tattheva bhagavato purato nisīdi.

"Yes, venerable sir," replied Venerable Cundaka to the Blessed One. He then spread out the fourfold outer robe. Then the Blessed One lay down on his right side in the lion's posture, placing one foot upon the other, mindful and fully aware, focusing on the thought of rising. Venerable Cundaka sat right there in front of the Blessed One.

Gantvāna buddho nadikaṃ kakudhaṃ,Acchodakaṃ sātudakaṃ vippasannaṃ;Ogāhi satthā akilantarūpo [sukilantarūpo (sī. pī.)],Tathāgato appaṭimo ca [appaṭimodha (pī.)] loke.

Having gone to the Kakudha River, The Buddha, with cool, drinkable, and very clear waters, The Teacher plunged in, unwearied in body, The Tathagata, without equal in the world.

Nhatvā ca pivitvā cudatāri satthā [pivitvā cundakena, pivitvā ca uttari (ka.)],Purakkhato bhikkhugaṇassa majjhe;Vattā [satthā (sī. syā. pī.)] pavattā bhagavā idha dhamme,Upāgami ambavanaṃ mahesi.

Having bathed and drunk, the Teacher emerged, Preceded by the assembly of bhikkhus; The Blessed One, the speaker and expounder of the Dhamma here, Approached the mango grove, the great sage.

Āmantayi cundakaṃ nāma bhikkhuṃ,Catugguṇaṃ santhara me nipajjaṃ;So codito bhāvitattena cundo,Catugguṇaṃ santhari khippameva.

He addressed the bhikkhu named Cunda, "Spread out a fourfold outer robe for me to lie on." Urged on by the Developed One, Cunda, Quickly spread out the fourfold outer robe.

Nipajji satthā akilantarūpo,Cundopi tattha pamukhe [samukhe (ka.)] nisīdīti.

The Teacher, unwearied in body, lay down, And Cunda too sat there in front of him.

197. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘siyā kho [yo kho (ka.)], panānanda, cundassa kammāraputtassa koci vippaṭisāraṃ uppādeyya – ‘tassa te, āvuso cunda, alābhā tassa te dulladdhaṃ, yassa te tathāgato pacchimaṃ piṇḍapātaṃ paribhuñjitvā parinibbuto’ti. Cundassa, ānanda, kammāraputtassa evaṃ vippaṭisāro paṭivinetabbo – ‘tassa te, āvuso cunda, lābhā tassa te suladdhaṃ, yassa te tathāgato pacchimaṃ piṇḍapātaṃ paribhuñjitvā parinibbuto. Sammukhā metaṃ, āvuso cunda, bhagavato sutaṃ sammukhā paṭiggahitaṃ – dve me piṇḍapātā samasamaphalā [samā samaphalā (ka.)] samavipākā [samasamavipākā (sī. syā. pī.)], ativiya aññehi piṇḍapātehi mahapphalatarā ca mahānisaṃsatarā ca. Katame dve? Yañca piṇḍapātaṃ paribhuñjitvā tathāgato anuttaraṃ sammāsambodhiṃ abhisambujjhati, yañca piṇḍapātaṃ paribhuñjitvā tathāgato anupādisesāya nibbānadhātuyā parinibbāyati. Ime dve piṇḍapātā samasamaphalā samavipākā, ativiya aññehi piṇḍapātehi mahapphalatarā ca mahānisaṃsatarā ca. Āyusaṃvattanikaṃ āyasmatā cundena kammāraputtena kammaṃ upacitaṃ, vaṇṇasaṃvattanikaṃ āyasmatā cundena kammāraputtena kammaṃ upacitaṃ, sukhasaṃvattanikaṃ āyasmatā cundena kammāraputtena kammaṃ upacitaṃ, yasasaṃvattanikaṃ āyasmatā cundena kammāraputtena kammaṃ upacitaṃ, saggasaṃvattanikaṃ āyasmatā cundena kammāraputtena kammaṃ upacitaṃ, ādhipateyyasaṃvattanikaṃ āyasmatā cundena kammāraputtena kammaṃ upacita’nti. Cundassa, ānanda, kammāraputtassa evaṃ vippaṭisāro paṭivinetabbo’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etamatthaṃ viditvā tāyaṃ velāyaṃ imaṃ udānaṃ udānesi –

197.Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Ānanda, it is possible that someone might arouse remorse in Cunda the smith's son, saying: ‘It is your loss, friend Cunda, it is your misfortune that the Tathāgata, having eaten his last alms-meal from you, attained final Nibbāna.’ Ānanda, the remorse of Cunda the smith's son should be dispelled thus: ‘It is your gain, friend Cunda, it is your good fortune that the Tathāgata, having eaten his last alms-meal from you, attained final Nibbāna. Friend Cunda, I have heard this face to face from the Blessed One, I have received it face to face: “These two alms-meals have equal fruit, equal result, and far surpass other alms-meals in great fruit and great benefit. Which two? The alms-meal after eating which the Tathāgata attains unsurpassed perfect enlightenment, and the alms-meal after eating which the Tathāgata attains final Nibbāna without any remainder of clinging. These two alms-meals have equal fruit, equal result, and far surpass other alms-meals in great fruit and great benefit. Venerable Cunda the smith's son has accumulated kamma leading to long life, has accumulated kamma leading to beauty, has accumulated kamma leading to happiness, has accumulated kamma leading to a large following, has accumulated kamma leading to heaven, has accumulated kamma leading to supremacy.” Ānanda, the remorse of Cunda the smith's son should be dispelled in this way." Then the Blessed One, having understood the meaning of this, on that occasion uttered this inspired utterance:

‘‘Dadato puññaṃ pavaḍḍhati,Saṃyamato veraṃ na cīyati;Kusalo ca jahāti pāpakaṃ,Rāgadosamohakkhayā sanibbuto’’ti.

Merit increases for the giver; Enmity is not amassed by the self-controlled; The skillful abandon evil; By the destruction of lust, hate, and delusion, one is at peace.

## Catuttho bhāṇavāro.

### The Fourth Recitation Section.

## Yamakasālā

### The Twin Sāla Trees

198. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘āyāmānanda, yena hiraññavatiyā nadiyā pārimaṃ tīraṃ, yena kusinārā upavattanaṃ mallānaṃ sālavanaṃ tenupasaṅkamissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi. Atha kho bhagavā mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ yena hiraññavatiyā nadiyā pārimaṃ tīraṃ, yena kusinārā upavattanaṃ mallānaṃ sālavanaṃ tenupasaṅkami. Upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘iṅgha me tvaṃ, ānanda, antarena yamakasālānaṃ uttarasīsakaṃ mañcakaṃ paññapehi, kilantosmi, ānanda, nipajjissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paṭissutvā antarena yamakasālānaṃ uttarasīsakaṃ mañcakaṃ paññapesi. Atha kho bhagavā dakkhiṇena passena sīhaseyyaṃ kappesi pāde pādaṃ accādhāya sato sampajāno.

198.Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Come, Ānanda, let us go to the farther bank of the Hiraññavatī River, to Kusinārā, to the Mallas' Upavattana sāla grove." "Yes, Venerable Sir," replied Venerable Ānanda to the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One, together with a large community of monks, went to the farther bank of the Hiraññavatī River, to Kusinārā, to the Mallas' Upavattana sāla grove. Upon arriving, he addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Please, Ānanda, prepare a bed for me between the twin sāla trees with its head to the north. I am tired, Ānanda, I will lie down." "Yes, Venerable Sir," replied Venerable Ānanda to the Blessed One and prepared a bed between the twin sāla trees with its head to the north. Then the Blessed One lay down on his right side in the lion's posture, overlapping one foot on the other, mindful and fully aware.

Tena kho pana samayena yamakasālā sabbaphāliphullā honti akālapupphehi. Te tathāgatassa sarīraṃ okiranti ajjhokiranti abhippakiranti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi mandāravapupphāni antalikkhā papatanti, tāni tathāgatassa sarīraṃ okiranti ajjhokiranti abhippakiranti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi candanacuṇṇāni antalikkhā papatanti, tāni tathāgatassa sarīraṃ okiranti ajjhokiranti abhippakiranti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi tūriyāni antalikkhe vajjanti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi saṅgītāni antalikkhe vattanti tathāgatassa pūjāya.

At that time, the twin sāla trees were in full bloom with flowers all over, even though it was not the season for flowering. They showered, sprinkled, and strewed the Tathāgata's body in homage to him. Divine coral-tree flowers fell from the sky, showering, sprinkling, and strewing the Tathāgata's body in homage to him. Divine sandalwood powder fell from the sky, showering, sprinkling, and strewing the Tathāgata's body in homage to him. Divine musical instruments played in the sky in homage to the Tathāgata. Divine songs resounded in the sky in homage to the Tathāgata.

199. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘sabbaphāliphullā kho, ānanda, yamakasālā akālapupphehi. Te tathāgatassa sarīraṃ okiranti ajjhokiranti abhippakiranti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi mandāravapupphāni antalikkhā papatanti, tāni tathāgatassa sarīraṃ okiranti ajjhokiranti abhippakiranti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi candanacuṇṇāni antalikkhā papatanti, tāni tathāgatassa sarīraṃ okiranti ajjhokiranti abhippakiranti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi tūriyāni antalikkhe vajjanti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Dibbānipi saṅgītāni antalikkhe vattanti tathāgatassa pūjāya. Na kho, ānanda, ettāvatā tathāgato sakkato vā hoti garukato vā mānito vā pūjito vā apacito vā. Yo kho, ānanda, bhikkhu vā bhikkhunī vā upāsako vā upāsikā vā dhammānudhammappaṭipanno viharati sāmīcippaṭipanno anudhammacārī, so tathāgataṃ sakkaroti garuṃ karoti māneti pūjeti apaciyati [idaṃ padaṃ sīsyāipotthakesu na dissati], paramāya pūjāya. Tasmātihānanda, dhammānudhammappaṭipannā viharissāma sāmīcippaṭipannā anudhammacārinoti. Evañhi vo, ānanda, sikkhitabba’’nti.

199.Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Ānanda, the twin sāla trees are in full bloom with unseasonal flowers. They shower, sprinkle, and strew the Tathāgata's body with flowers in homage to the Tathāgata. Divine coral-tree flowers fall from the sky, showering, sprinkling, and strewing the Tathāgata's body in homage to the Tathāgata. Divine sandalwood powder falls from the sky, showering, sprinkling, and strewing the Tathāgata's body in homage to the Tathāgata. Divine musical instruments play in the sky in homage to the Tathāgata. Divine songs resound in the sky in homage to the Tathāgata. Yet, Ānanda, the Tathāgata is not truly honored, revered, esteemed, worshipped, or venerated by this. But whoever—whether a monk, nun, layman, or laywoman—lives practicing the Dhamma in accordance with the Dhamma, practicing properly, living in conformity with the Dhamma, it is they who truly honor, revere, esteem, worship, and venerate the Tathāgata with the highest homage. Therefore, Ānanda, let us live practicing the Dhamma in accordance with the Dhamma, practicing properly, living in conformity with the Dhamma. Thus should you train yourselves, Ānanda."

## Upavāṇatthero

### The Elder Upavāṇa.

200. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā upavāṇo bhagavato purato ṭhito hoti bhagavantaṃ bījayamāno. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ upavāṇaṃ apasāresi – ‘‘apehi, bhikkhu, mā me purato aṭṭhāsī’’ti. Atha kho āyasmato ānandassa etadahosi – ‘‘ayaṃ kho āyasmā upavāṇo dīgharattaṃ bhagavato upaṭṭhāko santikāvacaro samīpacārī. Atha ca pana bhagavā pacchime kāle āyasmantaṃ upavāṇaṃ apasāreti – ‘apehi bhikkhu, mā me purato aṭṭhāsī’ti. Ko nu kho hetu, ko paccayo, yaṃ bhagavā āyasmantaṃ upavāṇaṃ apasāreti – ‘apehi, bhikkhu, mā me purato aṭṭhāsī’ti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘ayaṃ, bhante, āyasmā upavāṇo dīgharattaṃ bhagavato upaṭṭhāko santikāvacaro samīpacārī. Atha ca pana bhagavā pacchime kāle āyasmantaṃ upavāṇaṃ apasāreti – ‘‘apehi, bhikkhu, mā me purato aṭṭhāsī’’ti. Ko nu kho, bhante, hetu, ko paccayo, yaṃ bhagavā āyasmantaṃ upavāṇaṃ apasāreti – ‘‘apehi, bhikkhu, mā me purato aṭṭhāsī’’ti? ‘‘Yebhuyyena, ānanda, dasasu lokadhātūsu devatā sannipatitā tathāgataṃ dassanāya. Yāvatā, ānanda, kusinārā upavattanaṃ mallānaṃ sālavanaṃ samantato dvādasa yojanāni, natthi so padeso vālaggakoṭinitudanamattopi mahesakkhāhi devatāhi apphuṭo. Devatā, ānanda, ujjhāyanti – ‘dūrā ca vatamha āgatā tathāgataṃ dassanāya. Kadāci karahaci tathāgatā loke uppajjanti arahanto sammāsambuddhā. Ajjeva rattiyā pacchime yāme tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Ayañca mahesakkho bhikkhu bhagavato purato ṭhito ovārento, na mayaṃ labhāma pacchime kāle tathāgataṃ dassanāyā’’’ti.

200.At that time, Venerable Upavāṇa was standing in front of the Blessed One, fanning him. Then the Blessed One dismissed Venerable Upavāṇa, saying, "Get away, bhikkhu, do not stand in front of me." Then Venerable Ānanda thought, "This Venerable Upavāṇa has for a long time been an attendant of the Blessed One, living close by and in his presence. Yet now, in his final moments, the Blessed One dismisses Venerable Upavāṇa, saying, 'Get away, bhikkhu, do not stand in front of me.' What is the reason, what is the cause, for the Blessed One to dismiss Venerable Upavāṇa like this?" Then Venerable Ānanda said to the Blessed One, "Venerable sir, this Venerable Upavāṇa has for a long time been an attendant of the Blessed One, living close by and in his presence. Yet now, in his final moments, the Blessed One dismisses him, saying, 'Get away, bhikkhu, do not stand in front of me.' What, venerable sir, is the reason, what is the cause, for the Blessed One to dismiss Venerable Upavāṇa like this?" "Ānanda, for the most part, deities from the ten world-systems have assembled to see the Tathāgata. As far as Kusinārā, the Mallans' sāla grove, up to twelve yojanas all around, there is no space even the size of the prick of a hair-tip that is not touched by powerful deities. The deities, Ānanda, are complaining: 'Indeed, we have come from afar to see the Tathāgata. Only rarely do Tathāgatas arise in the world—worthy ones, Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones. Tonight, in the last watch of the night, the Tathāgata will attain final Nibbāna. And this powerful bhikkhu standing in front of the Blessed One is obstructing us, and we cannot see the Tathāgata in his final moments!'"

201. ‘‘Kathaṃbhūtā pana, bhante, bhagavā devatā manasikarotī’’ti [manasi karontīti (syā. ka.)]? ‘‘Santānanda, devatā ākāse pathavīsaññiniyo kese pakiriya kandanti, bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti [chinnaṃpādaṃviya papatanti (syā.)], āvaṭṭanti, vivaṭṭanti – ‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbāyissati, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbāyissati, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ [cakkhumā (syā. ka.)] loke antaradhaṃāyissatī’ti.

201."But how, Venerable Sir," asked Ānanda, "does the Blessed One regard the devas?" "There are, Ānanda, devas in the sky who are earth-perceiving; they throw down their hair and weep, they stretch out their arms and weep; they fall headlong, they roll over and over—'Too quickly the Blessed One will attain final Nibbāna, too quickly the Happy One will attain final Nibbāna, too quickly the Eye in the world will disappear!'"

‘‘Santānanda, devatā pathaviyaṃ pathavīsaññiniyo kese pakiriya kandanti, bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti, vivaṭṭanti – ‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbāyissati, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbāyissati, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antaradhāyissatī’’’ti.

"O Ānanda, the deities of the earth, with perceptions of earth, scatter their hair and weep, they stretch out their arms and weep, they fall prostrate, they roll over and over—'Too quickly will the Blessed One attain final Nibbāna, too quickly will the Well-gone One attain final Nibbāna, too quickly will the Eye in the world disappear!'"

‘‘Yā pana tā devatā vītarāgā, tā satā sampajānā adhivāsenti – ‘aniccā saṅkhārā, taṃ kutettha labbhā’ti.

"Those deities who are devoid of lust, mindful and fully aware, patiently endure, [thinking]: 'Impermanent are conditioned things; how could permanence be found here?'"

## Catusaṃvejanīyaṭṭhānāni

### The Four Places Inspiring Emotion

202. ‘‘Pubbe, bhante, disāsu vassaṃ vuṭṭhā [vassaṃvutthā (sī. syā. kaṃ. pī.)] bhikkhū āgacchanti tathāgataṃ dassanāya. Te mayaṃ labhāma manobhāvanīye bhikkhū dassanāya, labhāma payirupāsanāya. Bhagavato pana mayaṃ, bhante, accayena na labhissāma manobhāvanīye bhikkhū dassanāya, na labhissāma payirupāsanāyā’’ti.

202."Formerly, venerable sir, monks who had spent the rains in various regions would come to see the Tathāgata. We had the opportunity to see mentally inspiring monks and to attend upon them. But now, venerable sir, after the Blessed One's passing, we will no longer have the opportunity to see mentally inspiring monks or to attend upon them."

‘‘Cattārimāni, ānanda, saddhassa kulaputtassa dassanīyāni saṃvejanīyāni ṭhānāni. Katamāni cattāri? ‘Idha tathāgato jāto’ti, ānanda, saddhassa kulaputtassa dassanīyaṃ saṃvejanīyaṃ ṭhānaṃ. ‘Idha tathāgato anuttaraṃ sammāsambodhiṃ abhisambuddho’ti, ānanda, saddhassa kulaputtassa dassanīyaṃ saṃvejanīyaṃ ṭhānaṃ. ‘Idha tathāgatena anuttaraṃ dhammacakkaṃ pavattita’nti, ānanda, saddhassa kulaputtassa dassanīyaṃ saṃvejanīyaṃ ṭhānaṃ. ‘Idha tathāgato anupādisesāya nibbānadhātuyā parinibbuto’ti, ānanda, saddhassa kulaputtassa dassanīyaṃ saṃvejanīyaṃ ṭhānaṃ. Imāni kho, ānanda, cattāri saddhassa kulaputtassa dassanīyāni saṃvejanīyāni ṭhānāni.

"Ānanda, there are these four places that a faithful clansman should see, inspiring emotion. Which four? ‘Here the Tathāgata was born’—this, Ānanda, is a place that a faithful clansman should see, inspiring emotion. ‘Here the Tathāgata awakened to the supreme perfect enlightenment’—this, Ānanda, is a place that a faithful clansman should see, inspiring emotion. ‘Here the Tathāgata set in motion the unsurpassed Wheel of the Dhamma’—this, Ānanda, is a place that a faithful clansman should see, inspiring emotion. ‘Here the Tathāgata attained final Nibbāna in the Nibbāna-element without residue’—this, Ānanda, is a place that a faithful clansman should see, inspiring emotion. These, Ānanda, are the four places that a faithful clansman should see, inspiring emotion."

‘‘Āgamissanti kho, ānanda, saddhā bhikkhū bhikkhuniyo upāsakā upāsikāyo – ‘idha tathāgato jāto’tipi, ‘idha tathāgato anuttaraṃ sammāsambodhiṃ abhisambuddho’tipi, ‘idha tathāgatena anuttaraṃ dhammacakkaṃ pavattita’ntipi, ‘idha tathāgato anupādisesāya nibbānadhātuyā parinibbuto’tipi. Ye hi keci, ānanda, cetiyacārikaṃ āhiṇḍantā pasannacittā kālaṅkarissanti, sabbe te kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā sugatiṃ saggaṃ lokaṃ upapajjissantī’’ti.

"Faithful monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen will come, Ānanda, thinking: ‘Here the Tathāgata was born,’ ‘Here the Tathāgata awakened to the supreme perfect enlightenment,’ ‘Here the Tathāgata set in motion the unsurpassed Wheel of the Dhamma,’ ‘Here the Tathāgata attained final Nibbāna in the Nibbāna-element without residue.’ And whoever, Ānanda, while wandering on pilgrimage to these shrines, passes away with a serene heart, all of them, on the dissolution of the body, after death, will be reborn in a good destination, in the heavenly world."

## Ānandapucchākathā

### The Questions of Ānanda

203. ‘‘Kathaṃ mayaṃ, bhante, mātugāme paṭipajjāmā’’ti? ‘‘Adassanaṃ, ānandā’’ti. ‘‘Dassane, bhagavā, sati kathaṃ paṭipajjitabba’’nti? ‘‘Anālāpo, ānandā’’ti. ‘‘Ālapantena pana, bhante, kathaṃ paṭipajjitabba’’nti? ‘‘Sati, ānanda, upaṭṭhāpetabbā’’ti.

203."How, venerable sir, are we to conduct ourselves with regard to women?" "By not seeing them, Ānanda." "But if there is seeing, venerable sir, how are we to conduct ourselves?" "By not speaking, Ānanda." "But if we have to speak, venerable sir, how are we to conduct ourselves?" "Mindfulness should be established, Ānanda."

204. ‘‘Kathaṃ mayaṃ, bhante, tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjāmā’’ti? ‘‘Abyāvaṭā tumhe, ānanda, hotha tathāgatassa sarīrapūjāya. Iṅgha tumhe, ānanda, sāratthe ghaṭatha anuyuñjatha [sadatthe anuyuñjatha (sī. syā.), sadatthaṃ anuyuñjatha (pī.), sāratthe anuyuñjatha (ka.)], sāratthe appamattā ātāpino pahitattā viharatha. Santānanda, khattiyapaṇḍitāpi brāhmaṇapaṇḍitāpi gahapatipaṇḍitāpi tathāgate abhippasannā, te tathāgatassa sarīrapūjaṃ karissantī’’ti.

204."How, venerable sir, are we to proceed regarding the body of the Tathāgata?" "Do not concern yourselves, Ānanda, with the honoring of the Tathāgata's body. Rather, Ānanda, strive for the essential goal, devote yourselves to the essential goal; dwell heedful, ardent, and resolute. There are, Ānanda, wise nobles, wise brahmins, and wise householders who have deep faith in the Tathāgata—they will honor the Tathāgata's body."

205. ‘‘Kathaṃ pana, bhante, tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjitabba’’nti? ‘‘Yathā kho, ānanda, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjanti, evaṃ tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjitabba’’nti. ‘‘Kathaṃ pana, bhante, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjantī’’ti? ‘‘Rañño, ānanda, cakkavattissa sarīraṃ ahatena vatthena veṭhenti, ahatena vatthena veṭhetvā vihatena kappāsena veṭhenti, vihatena kappāsena veṭhetvā ahatena vatthena veṭhenti. Etenupāyena pañcahi yugasatehi rañño cakkavattissa sarīraṃ [sarīre (syā. ka.)] veṭhetvā āyasāya teladoṇiyā pakkhipitvā aññissā āyasāya doṇiyā paṭikujjitvā sabbagandhānaṃ citakaṃ karitvā rañño cakkavattissa sarīraṃ jhāpenti. Cātumahāpathe [cātummahāpathe (sī. syā. kaṃ. pī.)] rañño cakkavattissa thūpaṃ karonti. Evaṃ kho, ānanda, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjanti. Yathā kho, ānanda, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjanti, evaṃ tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjitabbaṃ. Cātumahāpathe tathāgatassa thūpo kātabbo. Tattha ye mālaṃ vā gandhaṃ vā cuṇṇakaṃ [vaṇṇakaṃ (sī. pī.)] vā āropessanti vā abhivādessanti vā cittaṃ vā pasādessanti tesaṃ taṃ bhavissati dīgharattaṃ hitāya sukhāya.

205."But how, venerable sir, should the Tathāgata's body be treated?" "Just as, Ānanda, the body of a universal monarch is treated, so should the Tathāgata's body be treated." "But how, venerable sir, is the body of a universal monarch treated?" "Ānanda, the body of a universal monarch is wrapped in new cloth; having wrapped it in new cloth, they wrap it with carded cotton; having wrapped it with carded cotton, they wrap it again with new cloth. In this way, the body of a universal monarch is wrapped in five hundred layers, then placed in a golden oil-trough and covered with another golden trough. A pyre of all kinds of fragrant woods is made, and the body of the universal monarch is cremated. At the four great crossroads, a stupa is built for the universal monarch. Thus, Ānanda, the body of a universal monarch is treated. Just as the body of a universal monarch is treated, so should the Tathāgata's body be treated. At the four great crossroads, a stupa should be built for the Tathāgata. There, whoever offers garlands, incense, or powder, or makes salutations, or inspires confidence in their mind, that will be for their long-term welfare and happiness."

## Thūpārahapuggalo

### Persons Worthy of a Stupa

206. ‘‘Cattārome, ānanda, thūpārahā. Katame cattāro? Tathāgato arahaṃ sammāsambuddho thūpāraho, paccekasambuddho thūpāraho, tathāgatassa sāvako thūpāraho, rājā cakkavattī [cakkavatti (syā. ka.)] thūpārahoti.

206."Ānanda, there are these four persons worthy of a stupa. Which four? The Tathāgata, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, is worthy of a stupa; a Paccekabuddha is worthy of a stupa; a disciple of the Tathāgata is worthy of a stupa; and a wheel-turning monarch is worthy of a stupa."

‘‘Kiñcānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca tathāgato arahaṃ sammāsambuddho thūpāraho? ‘Ayaṃ tassa bhagavato arahato sammāsambuddhassa thūpo’ti, ānanda, bahujanā cittaṃ pasādenti. Te tattha cittaṃ pasādetvā kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā sugatiṃ saggaṃ lokaṃ upapajjanti. Idaṃ kho, ānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca tathāgato arahaṃ sammāsambuddho thūpāraho.

"And on account of what benefit, Ānanda, is the Tathāgata, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, worthy of a stupa? 'This is the stupa of that Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One,' Ānanda, many people gain confidence in their minds. Having gained confidence there, with the breakup of the body, after death, they are reborn in a good destination, in a heavenly world. This, Ānanda, is the benefit on account of which the Tathāgata, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, is worthy of a stupa."

‘‘Kiñcānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca paccekasambuddho thūpāraho? ‘Ayaṃ tassa bhagavato paccekasambuddhassa thūpo’ti, ānanda, bahujanā cittaṃ pasādenti. Te tattha cittaṃ pasādetvā kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā sugatiṃ saggaṃ lokaṃ upapajjanti. Idaṃ kho, ānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca paccekasambuddho thūpāraho.

"And on account of what benefit, Ānanda, is a Paccekabuddha worthy of a stupa? 'This is the stupa of that Blessed One, the Paccekabuddha,' Ānanda, many people gain confidence in their minds. Having gained confidence there, with the breakup of the body, after death, they are reborn in a good destination, in a heavenly world. This, Ānanda, is the benefit on account of which a Paccekabuddha is worthy of a stupa."

‘‘Kiñcānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca tathāgatassa sāvako thūpāraho? ‘Ayaṃ tassa bhagavato arahato sammāsambuddhassa sāvakassa thūpo’ti ānanda, bahujanā cittaṃ pasādenti. Te tattha cittaṃ pasādetvā kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā sugatiṃ saggaṃ lokaṃ upapajjanti. Idaṃ kho, ānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca tathāgatassa sāvako thūpāraho.

"And on account of what benefit, Ānanda, is a disciple of the Tathāgata worthy of a stupa? 'This is the stupa of that Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One's disciple,' Ānanda, many people gain confidence in their minds. Having gained confidence there, with the breakup of the body, after death, they are reborn in a good destination, in a heavenly world. This, Ānanda, is the benefit on account of which a disciple of the Tathāgata is worthy of a stupa."

‘‘Kiñcānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca rājā cakkavattī thūpāraho? ‘Ayaṃ tassa dhammikassa dhammarañño thūpo’ti, ānanda, bahujanā cittaṃ pasādenti. Te tattha cittaṃ pasādetvā kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā sugatiṃ saggaṃ lokaṃ upapajjanti. Idaṃ kho, ānanda, atthavasaṃ paṭicca rājā cakkavattī thūpāraho. Ime kho, ānanda cattāro thūpārahā’’ti.

"And on account of what benefit, Ānanda, is a wheel-turning monarch worthy of a stupa? 'This is the stupa of that righteous king, that king of Dhamma,' Ānanda, many people gain confidence in their minds. Having gained confidence there, with the breakup of the body, after death, they are reborn in a good destination, in a heavenly world. This, Ānanda, is the benefit on account of which a wheel-turning monarch is worthy of a stupa. These, Ānanda, are the four persons worthy of a stupa."

## Ānandaacchariyadhammo

### The Amazing and Wondrous Qualities of Ānanda

207. Atha kho āyasmā ānando vihāraṃ pavisitvā kapisīsaṃ ālambitvā rodamāno aṭṭhāsi – ‘‘ahañca vatamhi sekho sakaraṇīyo, satthu ca me parinibbānaṃ bhavissati, yo mama anukampako’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘kahaṃ nu kho, bhikkhave, ānando’’ti? ‘‘Eso, bhante, āyasmā ānando vihāraṃ pavisitvā kapisīsaṃ ālambitvā rodamāno ṭhito – ‘ahañca vatamhi sekho sakaraṇīyo, satthu ca me parinibbānaṃ bhavissati, yo mama anukampako’’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā aññataraṃ bhikkhuṃ āmantesi – ‘‘ehi tvaṃ, bhikkhu, mama vacanena ānandaṃ āmantehi – ‘satthā taṃ, āvuso ānanda, āmantetī’’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho so bhikkhu bhagavato paṭissutvā yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘satthā taṃ, āvuso ānanda, āmantetī’’ti. ‘‘Evamāvuso’’ti kho āyasmā ānando tassa bhikkhuno paṭissutvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ bhagavā etadavoca – ‘‘alaṃ, ānanda, mā soci mā paridevi, nanu etaṃ, ānanda, mayā paṭikacceva akkhātaṃ – ‘sabbeheva piyehi manāpehi nānābhāvo vinābhāvo aññathābhāvo’; taṃ kutettha, ānanda, labbhā. Yaṃ taṃ jātaṃ bhūtaṃ saṅkhataṃ palokadhammaṃ, taṃ vata tathāgatassāpi sarīraṃ mā palujjī’ti netaṃ ṭhānaṃ vijjati. Dīgharattaṃ kho te, ānanda, tathāgato paccupaṭṭhito mettena kāyakammena hitena sukhena advayena appamāṇena, mettena vacīkammena hitena sukhena advayena appamāṇena, mettena manokammena hitena sukhena advayena appamāṇena. Katapuññosi tvaṃ, ānanda, padhānamanuyuñja, khippaṃ hohisi anāsavo’’ti.

207.Then Venerable Ānanda entered the monastery, leaned against the doorframe, and stood weeping: "Alas, I am still a learner with work to do, and my Teacher—who is so compassionate toward me—is about to pass away."Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: "Where, monks, is Ānanda?""Venerable sir, Venerable Ānanda has entered the monastery, leaned against the doorframe, and stands weeping: 'Alas, I am still a learner with work to do, and my Teacher—who is so compassionate toward me—is about to pass away.'"Then the Blessed One addressed a certain monk: "Go, monk, and in my name summon Ānanda: 'The Teacher calls you, friend Ānanda.'""Yes, venerable sir," that monk replied to the Blessed One. He went to Venerable Ānanda and said, "The Teacher calls you, friend Ānanda.""Yes, friend," Venerable Ānanda replied to that monk. He went to the Blessed One, paid homage, and sat down to one side.The Blessed One then said to Venerable Ānanda as he sat there: "Enough, Ānanda, do not grieve, do not lament. Have I not told you before, Ānanda, that all that is dear and beloved must change, vanish, and become otherwise? How could it be otherwise, Ānanda? That which is born, come into being, compounded, and subject to decay—how could it be possible that the Tathāgata’s body should not break up? Such a thing is impossible. For a long time, Ānanda, you have attended upon the Tathāgata with loving bodily action, beneficial, pleasant, undivided, and boundless; with loving verbal action, beneficial, pleasant, undivided, and boundless; with loving mental action, beneficial, pleasant, undivided, and boundless. You have made much merit, Ānanda. Apply yourself diligently, and you will soon be free from taints."

208. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘yepi te, bhikkhave, ahesuṃ atītamaddhānaṃ arahanto sammāsambuddhā, tesampi bhagavantānaṃ etapparamāyeva upaṭṭhākā ahesuṃ, seyyathāpi mayhaṃ ānando. Yepi te, bhikkhave, bhavissanti anāgatamaddhānaṃ arahanto sammāsambuddhā, tesampi bhagavantānaṃ etapparamāyeva upaṭṭhākā bhavissanti, seyyathāpi mayhaṃ ānando. Paṇḍito, bhikkhave, ānando; medhāvī, bhikkhave, ānando. Jānāti ‘ayaṃ kālo tathāgataṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamituṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ayaṃ kālo bhikkhunīnaṃ, ayaṃ kālo upāsakānaṃ, ayaṃ kālo upāsikānaṃ, ayaṃ kālo rañño rājamahāmattānaṃ titthiyānaṃ titthiyasāvakāna’nti.

208.Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: "Monks, whatever Arahants, Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones there were in the past, for those Blessed Ones too, their attendants were just like Ānanda is for me. And whatever Arahants, Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones there will be in the future, for those Blessed Ones too, their attendants will be just like Ānanda is for me. Ānanda is discerning, monks; Ānanda is intelligent. He knows: 'This is the time for monks to approach the Tathāgata for an audience; this is the time for nuns; this is the time for male lay followers; this is the time for female lay followers; this is the time for kings, royal ministers, other sectarians, and their disciples.'"

209. ‘‘Cattārome, bhikkhave, acchariyā abbhutā dhammā [abbhutadhammā (syā. ka.)] ānande. Katame cattāro? Sace, bhikkhave, bhikkhuparisā ānandaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce ānando dhammaṃ bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, bhikkhuparisā hoti, atha kho ānando tuṇhī hoti. Sace, bhikkhave, bhikkhunīparisā ānandaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce ānando dhammaṃ bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, bhikkhunīparisā hoti, atha kho ānando tuṇhī hoti. Sace, bhikkhave, upāsakaparisā ānandaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce ānando dhammaṃ bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, upāsakaparisā hoti, atha kho ānando tuṇhī hoti. Sace, bhikkhave, upāsikāparisā ānandaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce, ānando, dhammaṃ bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, upāsikāparisā hoti, atha kho ānando tuṇhī hoti. Ime kho, bhikkhave, cattāro acchariyā abbhutā dhammā ānande.

209."Monks, there are these four amazing and wondrous qualities in Ānanda. What four? If a company of monks approaches Ānanda to see him, they are delighted by the sight of him. If Ānanda speaks the Dhamma to them, they are delighted by his speech. And though the company of monks is not yet satisfied, Ānanda then becomes silent. If a company of nuns approaches Ānanda to see him, they are delighted by the sight of him. If Ānanda speaks the Dhamma to them, they are delighted by his speech. And though the company of nuns is not yet satisfied, Ānanda then becomes silent. If a company of male lay followers approaches Ānanda to see him, they are delighted by the sight of him. If Ānanda speaks the Dhamma to them, they are delighted by his speech. And though the company of male lay followers is not yet satisfied, Ānanda then becomes silent. If a company of female lay followers approaches Ānanda to see him, they are delighted by the sight of him. If Ānanda speaks the Dhamma to them, they are delighted by his speech. And though the company of female lay followers is not yet satisfied, Ānanda then becomes silent. These, monks, are the four amazing and wondrous qualities in Ānanda."

‘‘Cattārome, bhikkhave, acchariyā abbhutā dhammā raññe cakkavattimhi. Katame cattāro? Sace, bhikkhave, khattiyaparisā rājānaṃ cakkavattiṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce rājā cakkavattī bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, khattiyaparisā hoti. Atha kho rājā cakkavattī tuṇhī hoti. Sace bhikkhave, brāhmaṇaparisā…pe… gahapatiparisā…pe… samaṇaparisā rājānaṃ cakkavattiṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce rājā cakkavattī bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, samaṇaparisā hoti, atha kho rājā cakkavattī tuṇhī hoti. Evameva kho, bhikkhave, cattārome acchariyā abbhutā dhammā ānande. Sace, bhikkhave, bhikkhuparisā ānandaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce ānando dhammaṃ bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, bhikkhuparisā hoti. Atha kho ānando tuṇhī hoti. Sace, bhikkhave bhikkhunīparisā…pe… upāsakaparisā…pe… upāsikāparisā ānandaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamati, dassanena sā attamanā hoti. Tatra ce ānando dhammaṃ bhāsati, bhāsitenapi sā attamanā hoti. Atittāva, bhikkhave, upāsikāparisā hoti. Atha kho ānando tuṇhī hoti. Ime kho, bhikkhave, cattāro acchariyā abbhutā dhammā ānande’’ti.

"Monks, there are these four amazing and astonishing qualities in a wheel-turning monarch. What four? If, monks, an assembly of nobles approaches a wheel-turning monarch to see him, they are pleased by the sight. And if the wheel-turning monarch speaks, they are pleased by his speech. The assembly of nobles, monks, remains unsated. Then, the wheel-turning monarch remains silent. If, monks, an assembly of brahmins… an assembly of householders… an assembly of ascetics approaches a wheel-turning monarch to see him, they are pleased by the sight. And if the wheel-turning monarch speaks, they are pleased by his speech. The assembly of ascetics, monks, remains unsated. Then, the wheel-turning monarch remains silent. In the same way, monks, there are these four amazing and astonishing qualities in Ānanda. If, monks, an assembly of monks approaches Ānanda to see him, they are pleased by the sight.
