And if Ānanda speaks the Dhamma, they are pleased by his speech. The assembly of monks, monks, remains unsated. Then, Ānanda remains silent. If, monks, an assembly of nuns… an assembly of male lay followers… an assembly of female lay followers approaches Ānanda to see him, they are pleased by the sight. And if Ānanda speaks the Dhamma, they are pleased by his speech. The assembly of female lay followers, monks, remains unsated. Then, Ānanda remains silent. These, monks, are the four amazing and astonishing qualities in Ānanda."

## Mahāsudassanasuttadesanā

### The Great Sudassana Discourse

210. Evaṃ vutte āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘mā, bhante, bhagavā imasmiṃ khuddakanagarake ujjaṅgalanagarake sākhānagarake parinibbāyi. Santi, bhante, aññāni mahānagarāni, seyyathidaṃ – campā rājagahaṃ sāvatthī sāketaṃ kosambī bārāṇasī; ettha bhagavā parinibbāyatu. Ettha bahū khattiyamahāsālā, brāhmaṇamahāsālā gahapatimahāsālā tathāgate abhippasannā. Te tathāgatassa sarīrapūjaṃ karissantī’’ti ‘‘māhevaṃ, ānanda, avaca; māhevaṃ, ānanda, avaca – ‘khuddakanagarakaṃ ujjaṅgalanagarakaṃ sākhānagaraka’nti.

210.When this was said, Venerable Ānanda said to the Blessed One: "Lord, may the Blessed One not attain final Nibbāna in this little town, this town in the jungle, this branch town. There are, lord, other great cities, such as Campā, Rājagaha, Sāvatthī, Sāketa, Kosambī, Bārāṇasī; let the Blessed One attain final Nibbāna there. There, many wealthy nobles, wealthy brahmins, and wealthy householders have deep faith in the Tathāgata. They will attend to the Tathāgata's remains." "Do not speak thus, Ānanda. Do not speak thus, Ānanda, 'a little town, a town in the jungle, a branch town.'"

‘‘Bhūtapubbaṃ, ānanda, rājā mahāsudassano nāma ahosi cakkavattī dhammiko dhammarājā cāturanto vijitāvī janappadatthāvariyappatto sattaratanasamannāgato. Rañño, ānanda, mahāsudassanassa ayaṃ kusinārā kusāvatī nāma rājadhānī ahosi, puratthimena ca pacchimena ca dvādasayojanāni āyāmena; uttarena ca dakkhiṇena ca sattayojanāni vitthārena. Kusāvatī, ānanda, rājadhānī iddhā ceva ahosi phītā ca bahujanā ca ākiṇṇamanussā ca subhikkhā ca. Seyyathāpi, ānanda, devānaṃ āḷakamandā nāma rājadhānī iddhā ceva hoti phītā ca bahujanā ca ākiṇṇayakkhā ca subhikkhā ca; evameva kho, ānanda, kusāvatī rājadhānī iddhā ceva ahosi phītā ca bahujanā ca ākiṇṇamanussā ca subhikkhā ca. Kusāvatī, ānanda, rājadhānī dasahi saddehi avivittā ahosi divā ceva rattiñca, seyyathidaṃ – hatthisaddena assasaddena rathasaddena bherisaddena mudiṅgasaddena vīṇāsaddena gītasaddena saṅkhasaddena sammasaddena pāṇitāḷasaddena ‘asnātha pivatha khādathā’ti dasamena saddena.

Formerly, Ānanda, there was a king named Mahāsudassana, a wheel-turning monarch, a righteous king of Dhamma, conqueror of the four quarters, who had established the country in security, endowed with the seven treasures. And, Ānanda, for King Mahāsudassana, this Kusinārā was the royal capital called Kusāvatī, twelve leagues in length from east to west, and seven leagues in width from north to south. Kusāvatī, Ānanda, the royal capital, was prosperous and flourishing, populous and crowded with people, and well-supplied with food. Just as, Ānanda, the royal capital of the devas named Āḷakamandā is prosperous and flourishing, populous and crowded with yakkhas, and well-supplied with food, so too, Ānanda, Kusāvatī the royal capital was prosperous and flourishing, populous and crowded with people, and well-supplied with food. Kusāvatī, Ānanda, the royal capital, was never free of ten sounds by day or night—namely, the sound of elephants, the sound of horses, the sound of chariots, the sound of kettle drums, the sound of tabors, the sound of lutes, the sound of singing, the sound of conches, the sound of cymbals, the sound of hand-clapping, and the tenth sound: 'Eat, drink, consume!'

‘‘Gaccha tvaṃ, ānanda, kusināraṃ pavisitvā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ ārocehi – ‘ajja kho, vāseṭṭhā, rattiyā pacchime yāme tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Abhikkamatha vāseṭṭhā, abhikkamatha vāseṭṭhā. Mā pacchā vippaṭisārino ahuvattha – amhākañca no gāmakkhette tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ ahosi, na mayaṃ labhimhā pacchime kāle tathāgataṃ dassanāyā’’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paṭissutvā nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya attadutiyo kusināraṃ pāvisi.

"Go now, Ānanda, enter Kusinārā and announce to the Mallas of Kusinārā: ‘Tonight, Vāseṭṭhas, in the last watch of the night, the Tathāgata’s final Nibbāna will occur. Approach, Vāseṭṭhas, approach! Do not later regret it, thinking: "The Tathāgata’s final Nibbāna occurred in our own village territory, and we did not get to see the Tathāgata at his last moment."’” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied the Venerable Ānanda to the Blessed One. Then, having dressed and taken his bowl and outer robe, accompanied by another bhikkhu, he entered Kusinārā.

## Mallānaṃ vandanā

### The Mallas Pay Homage

211. Tena kho pana samayena kosinārakā mallā sandhāgāre [santhāgāre (sī. syā. pī.)] sannipatitā honti kenacideva karaṇīyena. Atha kho āyasmā ānando yena kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ sandhāgāraṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ ārocesi – ‘‘ajja kho, vāseṭṭhā, rattiyā pacchime yāme tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Abhikkamatha vāseṭṭhā abhikkamatha vāseṭṭhā. Mā pacchā vippaṭisārino ahuvattha – ‘amhākañca no gāmakkhette tathāgatassa parinibbānaṃ ahosi, na mayaṃ labhimhā pacchime kāle tathāgataṃ dassanāyā’’’ti. Idamāyasmato ānandassa vacanaṃ sutvā mallā ca mallaputtā ca mallasuṇisā ca mallapajāpatiyo ca aghāvino dummanā cetodukkhasamappitā appekacce kese pakiriya kandanti, bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti vivaṭṭanti – ‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbāyissati, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbāyissati, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antaradhāyissatī’ti. Atha kho mallā ca mallaputtā ca mallasuṇisā ca mallapajāpatiyo ca aghāvino dummanā cetodukkhasamappitā yena upavattanaṃ mallānaṃ sālavanaṃ yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkamiṃsu. Atha kho āyasmato ānandassa etadahosi – ‘‘sace kho ahaṃ kosinārake malle ekamekaṃ bhagavantaṃ vandāpessāmi, avandito bhagavā kosinārakehi mallehi bhavissati, athāyaṃ ratti vibhāyissati. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ kosinārake malle kulaparivattaso kulaparivattaso ṭhapetvā bhagavantaṃ vandāpeyyaṃ – ‘itthannāmo, bhante, mallo saputto sabhariyo sapariso sāmacco bhagavato pāde sirasā vandatī’ti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando kosinārake malle kulaparivattaso kulaparivattaso ṭhapetvā bhagavantaṃ vandāpesi – ‘itthannāmo, bhante, mallo saputto sabhariyo sapariso sāmacco bhagavato pāde sirasā vandatī’’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando etena upāyena paṭhameneva yāmena kosinārake malle bhagavantaṃ vandāpesi.

211.Now at that time the Mallas of Kusinārā had gathered in the assembly hall for some business. Then Venerable Ānanda approached the assembly hall of the Mallas of Kusinārā. Having approached, he announced to the Mallas of Kusinārā: "Today, Vāseṭṭhas, in the last watch of the night, the Tathāgata will attain final Nibbāna. Come forth, Vāseṭṭhas, come forth! Do not later regret it, thinking: 'The Tathāgata attained final Nibbāna in our own village territory, yet we did not get to see him at his last moment.'" Having heard Venerable Ānanda's words, the Mallas, their sons, daughters-in-law, wives, and people were distressed, sorrowful, and overcome with anguish. Some, tearing their hair, wept; some, raising their arms, wept; some fell down as if cut down; they rolled back and forth, lamenting: "Too soon the Blessed One will attain final Nibbāna! Too soon the Fortunate One will attain final Nibbāna! Too soon the Eye of the World will disappear!" Then the Mallas, their sons, daughters-in-law, wives, and people—distressed, sorrowful, and overcome with anguish—went to the sal grove of the Mallas at Upavattana, where Venerable Ānanda was. Then it occurred to Venerable Ānanda: "If I have the Mallas of Kusinārā pay homage to the Blessed One one by one, the Blessed One will not have been venerated by all the Mallas, and the night will be over. Why don't I arrange the Mallas of Kusinārā family by family, and then have them pay homage to the Blessed One, saying: 'Venerable sir, the Mallian named so-and-so, with his son, wife, retinue, and ministers, bows his head at the feet of the Blessed One.'" So Venerable Ānanda arranged the Mallas of Kusinārā family by family, and had them pay homage to the Blessed One, saying: "Venerable sir, the Mallian named so-and-so, with his son, wife, retinue, and ministers, bows his head at the feet of the Blessed One." Thus, by this means, Venerable Ānanda had all the Mallas of Kusinārā pay homage to the Blessed One during the first watch of the night.

## Subhaddaparibbājakavatthu

### The Story of the Wanderer Subhadda

212. Tena kho pana samayena subhaddo nāma paribbājako kusinārāyaṃ paṭivasati. Assosi kho subhaddo paribbājako – ‘‘ajja kira rattiyā pacchime yāme samaṇassa gotamassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissatī’’ti. Atha kho subhaddassa paribbājakassa etadahosi – ‘‘sutaṃ kho pana metaṃ paribbājakānaṃ vuḍḍhānaṃ mahallakānaṃ ācariyapācariyānaṃ bhāsamānānaṃ – ‘kadāci karahaci tathāgatā loke uppajjanti arahanto sammāsambuddhā’ti. Ajjeva rattiyā pacchime yāme samaṇassa gotamassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Atthi ca me ayaṃ kaṅkhādhammo uppanno, evaṃ pasanno ahaṃ samaṇe gotame, ‘pahoti me samaṇo gotamo tathā dhammaṃ desetuṃ, yathāhaṃ imaṃ kaṅkhādhammaṃ pajaheyya’’’nti. Atha kho subhaddo paribbājako yena upavattanaṃ mallānaṃ sālavanaṃ, yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sutaṃ metaṃ, bho ānanda, paribbājakānaṃ vuḍḍhānaṃ mahallakānaṃ ācariyapācariyānaṃ bhāsamānānaṃ – ‘kadāci karahaci tathāgatā loke uppajjanti arahanto sammāsambuddhā’ti. Ajjeva rattiyā pacchime yāme samaṇassa gotamassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Atthi ca me ayaṃ kaṅkhādhammo uppanno – evaṃ pasanno ahaṃ samaṇe gotame ‘pahoti me samaṇo gotamo tathā dhammaṃ desetuṃ, yathāhaṃ imaṃ kaṅkhādhammaṃ pajaheyya’nti. Sādhāhaṃ, bho ānanda, labheyyaṃ samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāyā’’ti. Evaṃ vutte āyasmā ānando subhaddaṃ paribbājakaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘alaṃ, āvuso subhadda, mā tathāgataṃ viheṭhesi, kilanto bhagavā’’ti. Dutiyampi kho subhaddo paribbājako…pe… tatiyampi kho subhaddo paribbājako āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sutaṃ metaṃ, bho ānanda, paribbājakānaṃ vuḍḍhānaṃ mahallakānaṃ ācariyapācariyānaṃ bhāsamānānaṃ – ‘kadāci karahaci tathāgatā loke uppajjanti arahanto sammāsambuddhā’ti. Ajjeva rattiyā pacchime yāme samaṇassa gotamassa parinibbānaṃ bhavissati. Atthi ca me ayaṃ kaṅkhādhammo uppanno – evaṃ pasanno ahaṃ samaṇe gotame, ‘pahoti me samaṇo gotamo tathā dhammaṃ desetuṃ, yathāhaṃ imaṃ kaṅkhādhammaṃ pajaheyya’nti. Sādhāhaṃ, bho ānanda, labheyyaṃ samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāyā’’ti. Tatiyampi kho āyasmā ānando subhaddaṃ paribbājakaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘alaṃ, āvuso subhadda, mā tathāgataṃ viheṭhesi, kilanto bhagavā’’ti.

212.Now at that time the wanderer Subhadda was staying at Kusinārā. The wanderer Subhadda heard: “Tonight, in the last watch of the night, the ascetic Gotama will attain final Nibbāna.” Then the wanderer Subhadda thought: “I have heard wanderers who are elders, senior, teachers of teachers, saying: ‘Only once in a long while do Tathāgatas arise in the world, Arahants, perfectly self-enlightened ones.’ Tonight, in the last watch of the night, the ascetic Gotama will attain final Nibbāna. And I have this doubt arisen: I have confidence in the ascetic Gotama, thinking: ‘The ascetic Gotama is capable of teaching me the Dhamma in such a way that I may abandon this doubt.’” Then the wanderer Subhadda went to the Mallians’ sal grove at Upavattana, where Venerable Ānanda was. Approaching Venerable Ānanda, he said: “Venerable Ānanda, I have heard wanderers who are elders, senior, teachers of teachers, saying: ‘Only once in a long while do Tathāgatas arise in the world, Arahants, perfectly self-enlightened ones.’ Tonight, in the last watch of the night, the ascetic Gotama will attain final Nibbāna. And I have this doubt arisen—I have confidence in the ascetic Gotama, thinking: ‘The ascetic Gotama is capable of teaching me the Dhamma in such a way that I may abandon this doubt.’ It would be good, friend Ānanda, if I could get to see the ascetic Gotama.” When this was said, Venerable Ānanda replied: “Enough, friend Subhadda, do not trouble the Tathāgata. The Blessed One is weary.” A second time, Subhadda the wanderer made the same request… A third time, Subhadda the wanderer said: “Venerable Ānanda, I have heard wanderers who are elders, senior, teachers of teachers, saying: ‘Only once in a long while do Tathāgatas arise in the world, Arahants, perfectly self-enlightened ones.’ Tonight, in the last watch of the night, the ascetic Gotama will attain final Nibbāna. And I have this doubt arisen—I have confidence in the ascetic Gotama, thinking: ‘The ascetic Gotama is capable of teaching me the Dhamma in such a way that I may abandon this doubt.’ It would be good, friend Ānanda, if I could get to see the ascetic Gotama.” A third time, Venerable Ānanda replied: “Enough, friend Subhadda, do not trouble the Tathāgata. The Blessed One is weary.”

213. Assosi kho bhagavā āyasmato ānandassa subhaddena paribbājakena saddhiṃ imaṃ kathāsallāpaṃ. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘alaṃ, ānanda, mā subhaddaṃ vāresi, labhataṃ, ānanda, subhaddo tathāgataṃ dassanāya. Yaṃ kiñci maṃ subhaddo pucchissati, sabbaṃ taṃ aññāpekkhova pucchissati, no vihesāpekkho. Yaṃ cassāhaṃ puṭṭho byākarissāmi, taṃ khippameva ājānissatī’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando subhaddaṃ paribbājakaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘gacchāvuso subhadda, karoti te bhagavā okāsa’’nti. Atha kho subhaddo paribbājako yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavatā saddhiṃ sammodi, sammodanīyaṃ kathaṃ sāraṇīyaṃ vītisāretvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho subhaddo paribbājako bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘yeme, bho gotama, samaṇabrāhmaṇā saṅghino gaṇino gaṇācariyā ñātā yasassino titthakarā sādhusammatā bahujanassa, seyyathidaṃ – pūraṇo kassapo, makkhali gosālo, ajito kesakambalo, pakudho kaccāyano, sañcayo belaṭṭhaputto, nigaṇṭho nāṭaputto, sabbete sakāya paṭiññāya abbhaññiṃsu, sabbeva na abbhaññiṃsu, udāhu ekacce abbhaññiṃsu, ekacce na abbhaññiṃsū’’ti? ‘‘Alaṃ, subhadda, tiṭṭhatetaṃ – ‘sabbete sakāya paṭiññāya abbhaññiṃsu, sabbeva na abbhaññiṃsu, udāhu ekacce abbhaññiṃsu, ekacce na abbhaññiṃsū’ti. Dhammaṃ te, subhadda, desessāmi; taṃ suṇāhi sādhukaṃ manasikarohi, bhāsissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho subhaddo paribbājako bhagavato paccassosi. Bhagavā etadavoca –

213.Now the Blessed One heard the conversation between Venerable Ānanda and the wanderer Subhadda. Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: “Enough, Ānanda, do not prevent Subhadda. Let Subhadda, Ānanda, have the opportunity to see the Tathāgata. Whatever Subhadda asks me, he will ask with the intention of understanding, not with the intention of causing trouble. Whatever I answer when asked, he will quickly understand.” Then Venerable Ānanda said to the wanderer Subhadda: “Go, friend Subhadda, the Blessed One grants you permission.” Then the wanderer Subhadda approached the Blessed One; having approached, he exchanged greetings with the Blessed One, and after exchanging courteous and amiable conversation, he sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the wanderer Subhadda said to the Blessed One: “Master Gotama, those ascetics and brahmins who are leaders of groups, heads of followings, teachers of followings, well-known, famous, founders of doctrines, esteemed as good by many people—such as Pūraṇa Kassapa, Makkhali Gosāla, Ajita Kesakambalo, Pakudha Kaccāyano, Sañjaya Belaṭṭhaputto, and Nigaṇṭha Nātaputto—did all of them realize according to their claims, or did none of them realize it, or did some realize it and some not?” “Enough, Subhadda, let that be—‘Did all of them realize according to their claims, or did none of them realize it, or did some realize it and some not?’ I will teach you the Dhamma, Subhadda; listen carefully and pay close attention, I will speak.” “Yes, venerable sir,” the wanderer Subhadda replied to the Blessed One. The Blessed One said:

214. ‘‘Yasmiṃ kho, subhadda, dhammavinaye ariyo aṭṭhaṅgiko maggo na upalabbhati, samaṇopi tattha na upalabbhati. Dutiyopi tattha samaṇo na upalabbhati. Tatiyopi tattha samaṇo na upalabbhati. Catutthopi tattha samaṇo na upalabbhati. Yasmiñca kho, subhadda, dhammavinaye ariyo aṭṭhaṅgiko maggo upalabbhati, samaṇopi tattha upalabbhati, dutiyopi tattha samaṇo upalabbhati, tatiyopi tattha samaṇo upalabbhati, catutthopi tattha samaṇo upalabbhati. Imasmiṃ kho, subhadda, dhammavinaye ariyo aṭṭhaṅgiko maggo upalabbhati, idheva, subhadda, samaṇo, idha dutiyo samaṇo, idha tatiyo samaṇo, idha catuttho samaṇo, suññā parappavādā samaṇebhi aññehi [aññe (pī.)]. Ime ca [idheva (ka.)], subhadda, bhikkhū sammā vihareyyuṃ, asuñño loko arahantehi assāti.

214.“Subhadda, in whatever teaching and discipline the Noble Eightfold Path is not found, neither a first ascetic is found, nor a second ascetic is found, nor a third ascetic is found, nor a fourth ascetic is found. But in whatever teaching and discipline the Noble Eightfold Path is found, a first ascetic is found, a second ascetic is found, a third ascetic is found, a fourth ascetic is found. In this teaching and discipline, Subhadda, the Noble Eightfold Path is found. Here alone, Subhadda, is a first ascetic, here a second ascetic, here a third ascetic, here a fourth ascetic. Other doctrines are empty of ascetics. But if these monks, Subhadda, were to live rightly, the world would not be devoid of Arahants.”

‘‘Ekūnatiṃso vayasā subhadda,Yaṃ pabbajiṃ kiṃkusalānuesī;Vassāni paññāsa samādhikāni,Yato ahaṃ pabbajito subhadda.

“At twenty-nine years of age, Subhadda, I went forth seeking what is wholesome. Fifty years and more have passed since I went forth, Subhadda.

Ñāyassa dhammassa padesavattī,Ito bahiddhā samaṇopi natthi.

One who practices a portion of the Noble Dhamma, outside of this there is no true ascetic.”

‘‘Dutiyopi samaṇo natthi. Tatiyopi samaṇo natthi. Catutthopi samaṇo natthi. Suññā parappavādā samaṇebhi aññehi. Ime ca, subhadda, bhikkhū sammā vihareyyuṃ, asuñño loko arahantehi assā’’ti.

“There is no second ascetic. There is no third ascetic. There is no fourth ascetic. Other doctrines are empty of ascetics. But if these monks, Subhadda, were to live rightly, the world would not be devoid of Arahants.”

215. Evaṃ vutte subhaddo paribbājako bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante, abhikkantaṃ, bhante. Seyyathāpi, bhante, nikkujjitaṃ vā ukkujjeyya, paṭicchannaṃ vā vivareyya, mūḷhassa vā maggaṃ ācikkheyya, andhakāre vā telapajjotaṃ dhāreyya, ‘cakkhumanto rūpāni dakkhantī’ti, evamevaṃ bhagavatā anekapariyāyena dhammo pakāsito. Esāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi dhammañca bhikkhusaṅghañca. Labheyyāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyaṃ upasampada’’nti. ‘‘Yo kho, subhadda, aññatitthiyapubbo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye ākaṅkhati pabbajjaṃ, ākaṅkhati upasampadaṃ, so cattāro māse parivasati. Catunnaṃ māsānaṃ accayena āraddhacittā bhikkhū pabbājenti upasampādenti bhikkhubhāvāya. Api ca mettha puggalavemattatā viditā’’ti. ‘‘Sace, bhante, aññatitthiyapubbā imasmiṃ dhammavinaye ākaṅkhantā pabbajjaṃ ākaṅkhantā upasampadaṃ cattāro māse parivasanti, catunnaṃ māsānaṃ accayena āraddhacittā bhikkhū pabbājenti upasampādenti bhikkhubhāvāya. Ahaṃ cattāri vassāni parivasissāmi, catunnaṃ vassānaṃ accayena āraddhacittā bhikkhū pabbājentu upasampādentu bhikkhubhāvāyā’’ti.

215.When this was said, the wanderer Subhadda said to the Blessed One: “Excellent, venerable sir! Excellent, venerable sir! Just as, venerable sir, one might set upright what had been overturned, or reveal what was hidden, or show the way to one who was lost, or hold up a lamp in the darkness, thinking, ‘Those with eyes will see forms,’ so in the same way has the Blessed One made the Dhamma clear in many ways. I go to the Blessed One for refuge, to the Dhamma, and to the Saṅgha of monks. May I receive the going forth in the Blessed One’s presence, may I receive the higher ordination.” “Subhadda, if someone who was formerly a member of another sect wishes for the going forth and wishes for the higher ordination in this Dhamma and Discipline, he must undergo probation for four months. At the end of the four months, if the monks are satisfied, they give him the going forth and the higher ordination into the state of monkhood. However, individual differences are recognized in this matter.” “If, venerable sir, those who were formerly members of other sects, wishing for the going forth and higher ordination in this Dhamma and Discipline, undergo probation for four months, and after the four months, if the monks are satisfied, they give them the going forth and higher ordination into the state of monkhood, then I will undergo probation for four years. At the end of the four years, if the monks are satisfied, let them give me the going forth and the higher ordination into the state of monkhood.”

Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘tenahānanda, subhaddaṃ pabbājehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paccassosi. Atha kho subhaddo paribbājako āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘lābhā vo, āvuso ānanda; suladdhaṃ vo, āvuso ānanda, ye ettha satthu [satthārā (syā.)] sammukhā antevāsikābhisekena abhisittā’’ti. Alattha kho subhaddo paribbājako bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, alattha upasampadaṃ. Acirūpasampanno kho panāyasmā subhaddo eko vūpakaṭṭho appamatto ātāpī pahitatto viharanto nacirasseva – ‘yassatthāya kulaputtā sammadeva agārasmā anagāriyaṃ pabbajanti’ tadanuttaraṃ brahmacariyapariyosānaṃ diṭṭheva dhamme sayaṃ abhiññā sacchikatvā upasampajja vihāsi. ‘Khīṇā jāti, vusitaṃ brahmacariyaṃ, kataṃ karaṇīyaṃ, nāparaṃ itthattāyā’ti abbhaññāsi. Aññataro kho panāyasmā subhaddo arahataṃ ahosi. So bhagavato pacchimo sakkhisāvako ahosīti.

Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: “Then, Ānanda, ordain Subhadda.” “Yes, Venerable Sir,” Venerable Ānanda replied to the Blessed One. Then the wanderer Subhadda said to Venerable Ānanda: “It is a gain for you, friend Ānanda; it is well gained for you, friend Ānanda, that you have been consecrated as a disciple in the Teacher’s presence.” Subhadda the wanderer received the going forth in the presence of the Blessed One, and he received the higher ordination. Not long after his higher ordination, Venerable Subhadda, dwelling alone, secluded, diligent, ardent, and resolute, soon realized for himself with direct knowledge, in this very life, the unsurpassed culmination of the holy life for which clansmen rightly go forth from the household life into homelessness, and having attained it, he remained. He directly knew: “Birth is destroyed, the holy life has been lived, what had to be done has been done, there is no more for this state of being.” And Venerable Subhadda became one of the arahants. He was the last direct disciple of the Blessed One.

## Pañcamo bhāṇavāro.

### The Fifth Recitation Section.

## Tathāgatapacchimavācā

### The Tathāgata's Last Words

216. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘siyā kho panānanda, tumhākaṃ evamassa – ‘atītasatthukaṃ pāvacanaṃ, natthi no satthā’ti. Na kho panetaṃ, ānanda, evaṃ daṭṭhabbaṃ. Yo vo, ānanda, mayā dhammo ca vinayo ca desito paññatto, so vo mamaccayena satthā. Yathā kho panānanda, etarahi bhikkhū aññamaññaṃ āvusovādena samudācaranti, na kho mamaccayena evaṃ samudācaritabbaṃ. Theratarena, ānanda, bhikkhunā navakataro bhikkhu nāmena vā gottena vā āvusovādena vā samudācaritabbo. Navakatarena bhikkhunā therataro bhikkhu ‘bhante’ti vā ‘āyasmā’ti vā samudācaritabbo. Ākaṅkhamāno, ānanda, saṅgho mamaccayena khuddānukhuddakāni sikkhāpadāni samūhanatu. Channassa, ānanda, bhikkhuno mamaccayena brahmadaṇḍo dātabbo’’ti. ‘‘Katamo pana, bhante, brahmadaṇḍo’’ti? ‘‘Channo, ānanda, bhikkhu yaṃ iccheyya, taṃ vadeyya. So bhikkhūhi neva vattabbo, na ovaditabbo, na anusāsitabbo’’ti.

216.Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: “Ānanda, it may be that you think: ‘The Teacher's instruction has ceased, now we have no Teacher!’ But it should not be seen like this, Ānanda. The Dhamma and the Discipline that I have taught and laid down for you, that will be your Teacher after I am gone. And, Ānanda, whereas now the monks address each other by the address ‘friend,’ after I am gone they should not do so. A senior monk, Ānanda, should address a junior monk by his name, his clan name, or as ‘friend,’ and a junior monk should address a senior monk as ‘Venerable Sir’ or ‘Venerable.’ If the Saṅgha wishes, after I am gone, it may abolish the minor and lesser training rules. And, Ānanda, after I am gone, the brahma-penalty should be imposed on the monk Channa.” “But what, Venerable Sir, is the brahma-penalty?” “Ānanda, whatever the monk Channa may wish to say, he should not be spoken to, admonished, or instructed by the monks.”

217. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘siyā kho pana, bhikkhave, ekabhikkhussāpi kaṅkhā vā vimati vā buddhe vā dhamme vā saṅghe vā magge vā paṭipadāya vā, pucchatha, bhikkhave, mā pacchā vippaṭisārino ahuvattha – ‘sammukhībhūto no satthā ahosi, na mayaṃ sakkhimhā bhagavantaṃ sammukhā paṭipucchitu’’’ nti. Evaṃ vutte te bhikkhū tuṇhī ahesuṃ. Dutiyampi kho bhagavā…pe… tatiyampi kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘siyā kho pana, bhikkhave, ekabhikkhussāpi kaṅkhā vā vimati vā buddhe vā dhamme vā saṅghe vā magge vā paṭipadāya vā, pucchatha, bhikkhave, mā pacchā vippaṭisārino ahuvattha – ‘sammukhībhūto no satthā ahosi, na mayaṃ sakkhimhā bhagavantaṃ sammukhā paṭipucchitu’’’ nti. Tatiyampi kho te bhikkhū tuṇhī ahesuṃ. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘siyā kho pana, bhikkhave, satthugāravenapi na puccheyyātha. Sahāyakopi, bhikkhave, sahāyakassa ārocetū’’ti. Evaṃ vutte te bhikkhū tuṇhī ahesuṃ. Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘acchariyaṃ, bhante, abbhutaṃ, bhante, evaṃ pasanno ahaṃ, bhante, imasmiṃ bhikkhusaṅghe, ‘natthi ekabhikkhussāpi kaṅkhā vā vimati vā buddhe vā dhamme vā saṅghe vā magge vā paṭipadāya vā’’’ti. ‘‘Pasādā kho tvaṃ, ānanda, vadesi, ñāṇameva hettha, ānanda, tathāgatassa. Natthi imasmiṃ bhikkhusaṅghe ekabhikkhussāpi kaṅkhā vā vimati vā buddhe vā dhamme vā saṅghe vā magge vā paṭipadāya vā. Imesañhi, ānanda, pañcannaṃ bhikkhusatānaṃ yo pacchimako bhikkhu, so sotāpanno avinipātadhammo niyato sambodhiparāyaṇo’’ti.

217.Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: “Monks, should even a single monk have any doubt or uncertainty about the Buddha, the Dhamma, the Saṅgha, the path, or the practice, ask now, monks. Do not later regret it, thinking: ‘The Teacher was face to face with us, yet we were not able to ask the Blessed One directly.’” When this was said, the monks remained silent. A second time the Blessed One addressed the monks… A third time the Blessed One addressed the monks: “Monks, should even a single monk have any doubt or uncertainty about the Buddha, the Dhamma, the Saṅgha, the path, or the practice, ask now, monks. Do not later regret it, thinking: ‘The Teacher was face to face with us, yet we were not able to ask the Blessed One directly.’” A third time the monks remained silent. Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: “Monks, perhaps you do not ask out of reverence for the Teacher. Then, monks, let one friend tell another.” When this was said, the monks remained silent. Then Venerable Ānanda said to the Blessed One: “It is wonderful, Venerable Sir, it is marvelous! I am so confident, Venerable Sir, regarding this community of monks, that not even a single monk has any doubt or uncertainty about the Buddha, the Dhamma, the Saṅgha, the path, or the practice.” “Ānanda, you speak out of confidence, but here, Ānanda, the Tathāgata has knowledge. In this community of monks, there is not even a single monk who has any doubt or uncertainty about the Buddha, the Dhamma, the Saṅgha, the path, or the practice. For, Ānanda, the last of these five hundred monks is a stream-enterer, not subject to falling away, assured, destined for enlightenment.”

218. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘handa dāni, bhikkhave, āmantayāmi vo, vayadhammā saṅkhārā appamādena sampādethā’’ti. Ayaṃ tathāgatassa pacchimā vācā.

218.Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: “Now, monks, I exhort you: all conditioned things are subject to decay. Accomplish with diligence!” This was the Tathāgata’s last word.

## Parinibbutakathā

### The Account of the Final Nibbāna

219. Atha kho bhagavā paṭhamaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, paṭhamajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā dutiyaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, dutiyajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā tatiyaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, tatiyajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā catutthaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji. Catutthajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā ākāsānañcāyatanaṃ samāpajji, ākāsānañcāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā viññāṇañcāyatanaṃ samāpajji, viññāṇañcāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā ākiñcaññāyatanaṃ samāpajji, ākiñcaññāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā nevasaññānāsaññāyatanaṃ samāpajji, nevasaññānāsaññāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā saññāvedayitanirodhaṃ samāpajji.

219.Then the Blessed One entered the first jhana. Emerging from the first jhana, he entered the second jhana. Emerging from the second jhana, he entered the third jhana. Emerging from the third jhana, he entered the fourth jhana. Emerging from the fourth jhana, he entered the base of infinite space. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite space, he entered the base of infinite consciousness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite consciousness, he entered the base of nothingness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of nothingness, he entered the base of neither perception nor non-perception. Emerging from the attainment of the base of neither perception nor non-perception, he entered the cessation of perception and feeling.

Atha kho āyasmā ānando āyasmantaṃ anuruddhaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘parinibbuto, bhante anuruddha, bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Nāvuso ānanda, bhagavā parinibbuto, saññāvedayitanirodhaṃ samāpanno’’ti.

Then the Venerable Ānanda said to the Venerable Anuruddha: "Venerable Anuruddha, has the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna?" "No, friend Ānanda, the Blessed One has not passed away into final Nibbāna; he has entered the cessation of perception and feeling."

Atha kho bhagavā saññāvedayitanirodhasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā nevasaññānāsaññāyatanaṃ samāpajji, nevasaññānāsaññāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā ākiñcaññāyatanaṃ samāpajji, ākiñcaññāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā viññāṇañcāyatanaṃ samāpajji, viññāṇañcāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā ākāsānañcāyatanaṃ samāpajji, ākāsānañcāyatanasamāpattiyā vuṭṭhahitvā catutthaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, catutthajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā tatiyaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, tatiyajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā dutiyaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, dutiyajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā paṭhamaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, paṭhamajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā dutiyaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, dutiyajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā tatiyaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, tatiyajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā catutthaṃ jhānaṃ samāpajji, catutthajjhānā vuṭṭhahitvā samanantarā bhagavā parinibbāyi.

Then the Blessed One, emerging from the attainment of the cessation of perception and feeling, entered the base of neither perception nor non-perception. Emerging from the attainment of the base of neither perception nor non-perception, he entered the base of nothingness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of nothingness, he entered the base of infinite consciousness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite consciousness, he entered the base of infinite space. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite space, he entered the fourth jhana. Emerging from the fourth jhana, he entered the third jhana. Emerging from the third jhana, he entered the second jhana. Emerging from the second jhana, he entered the first jhana. Emerging from the first jhana, he entered the second jhana. Emerging from the second jhana, he entered the third jhana. Emerging from the third jhana, he entered the fourth jhana. Emerging from the fourth jhana, the Blessed One immediately passed away into final Nibbāna.

220. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbānā mahābhūmicālo ahosi bhiṃsanako salomahaṃso. Devadundubhiyo ca phaliṃsu. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbānā brahmāsahampati imaṃ gāthaṃ abhāsi –

220.When the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna, simultaneously with his passing away into final Nibbāna there was a great earthquake, dreadful and hair-raising, and the drums of the gods resounded. When the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna, simultaneously with his passing away into final Nibbāna, Brahmā Sahampati recited this verse:

‘‘Sabbeva nikkhipissanti, bhūtā loke samussayaṃ;Yattha etādiso satthā, loke appaṭipuggalo;Tathāgato balappatto, sambuddho parinibbuto’’ti.

"All beings in the world will lay down this accumulation. Where even such a Teacher, without a peer in the world, the Tathāgata, possessed of strength, the Perfectly Enlightened One, has passed away into final Nibbāna!"

221. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbānā sakko devānamindo imaṃ gāthaṃ abhāsi –

221.When the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna, simultaneously with his passing away into final Nibbāna, Sakka, the ruler of the gods, uttered this verse:

‘‘Aniccā vata saṅkhārā, uppādavayadhammino;Uppajjitvā nirujjhanti, tesaṃ vūpasamo sukho’’ti.

"Impermanent, indeed, are conditioned things, subject to arising and passing away. Having arisen, they cease; their stilling is bliss."

222. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbānā āyasmā anuruddho imā gāthāyo abhāsi –

222.When the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna, simultaneously with his passing away into final Nibbāna, the Venerable Anuruddha recited these verses:

‘‘Nāhu assāsapassāso, ṭhitacittassa tādino;Anejo santimārabbha, yaṃ kālamakarī muni.

"There was no in-breath or out-breath for that steadfast one, whose mind was still; craving gone, attaining peace, the sage has completed his time."

‘‘Asallīnena cittena, vedanaṃ ajjhavāsayi;Pajjotasseva nibbānaṃ, vimokkho cetaso ahū’’ti.

"With unwavering mind, he endured feeling. Like the extinguishing of a lamp, there was liberation of his mind."

223. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbānā āyasmā ānando imaṃ gāthaṃ abhāsi –

223.When the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna, simultaneously with his passing away into final Nibbāna, the Venerable Ānanda recited this verse:

‘‘Tadāsi yaṃ bhiṃsanakaṃ, tadāsi lomahaṃsanaṃ;Sabbākāravarūpete, sambuddhe parinibbute’’ti.

"Then there was terror, then there was horripilation, when the Perfectly Enlightened One, endowed with all excellent qualities, passed away into final Nibbāna."

224. Parinibbute bhagavati ye te tattha bhikkhū avītarāgā appekacce bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti vivaṭṭanti, ‘‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antarahito’’ti. Ye pana te bhikkhū vītarāgā, te satā sampajānā adhivāsenti – ‘‘aniccā saṅkhārā, taṃ kutettha labbhā’’ti.

224.When the Blessed One had passed away into final Nibbāna, some monks there who were not free from passion stretched out their arms and wept, collapsed, rolled back and forth, lamenting, "Too soon the Blessed One has passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon the Sublime One has passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon the Eye has disappeared from the world!" But those monks who were free from passion, mindful and fully aware, endured, reflecting that "Impermanent are conditioned things; how could it be otherwise?"

225. Atha kho āyasmā anuruddho bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘alaṃ, āvuso, mā socittha mā paridevittha. Nanu etaṃ, āvuso, bhagavatā paṭikacceva akkhātaṃ – ‘sabbeheva piyehi manāpehi nānābhāvo vinābhāvo aññathābhāvo’. Taṃ kutettha, āvuso, labbhā. ‘Yaṃ taṃ jātaṃ bhūtaṃ saṅkhataṃ palokadhammaṃ, taṃ vata mā palujjī’ti, netaṃ ṭhānaṃ vijjati. Devatā, āvuso, ujjhāyantī’’ti. ‘‘Kathaṃbhūtā pana, bhante, āyasmā anuruddho devatā manasi karotī’’ti [bhante anuruddha devatā manasi karontīti (syā. ka.)]?

225.Then Venerable Anuruddha addressed the monks: "Enough, friends, do not grieve, do not lament. Has not the Blessed One declared this beforehand: 'All that is dear and beloved is subject to separation, to change, to otherness'? Where could this be found, friends, that what is born, become, conditioned, subject to decay, should not decay? Such a thing is not possible. The deities, friends, are murmuring." "But what kind of deities, Venerable Anuruddha, are you attending to in your mind?"

‘‘Santāvuso ānanda, devatā ākāse pathavīsaññiniyo kese pakiriya kandanti, bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti, vivaṭṭanti – ‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antarahito’ti. Santāvuso ānanda, devatā pathaviyā pathavīsaññiniyo kese pakiriya kandanti, bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti, vivaṭṭanti – ‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antarahito’ti. Yā pana tā devatā vītarāgā, tā satā sampajānā adhivāsenti – ‘aniccā saṅkhārā, taṃ kutettha labbhā’ti. Atha kho āyasmā ca anuruddho āyasmā ca ānando taṃ rattāvasesaṃ dhammiyā kathāya vītināmesuṃ.

"Friend Ananda, there are deities in the sky who perceive the earth, tearing their hair, wailing, raising their arms, falling down as if cut down, rolling and tossing about, crying: 'Too soon has the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Sublime One passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Eye of the World vanished!' Friend Ananda, there are deities on the earth who perceive the earth, tearing their hair, wailing, raising their arms, falling down as if cut down, rolling and tossing about, crying: 'Too soon has the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Sublime One passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Eye of the World vanished!' But those deities who are free from passion remain mindful and composed, reflecting: 'Impermanent are conditioned things; how could it be otherwise?' Then the Venerable Anuruddha and the Venerable Ananda spent the rest of the night in religious discussion."

226. Atha kho āyasmā anuruddho āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘gacchāvuso ānanda, kusināraṃ pavisitvā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ ārocehi – ‘parinibbuto, vāseṭṭhā, bhagavā, yassadāni kālaṃ maññathā’’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho āyasmā ānando āyasmato anuruddhassa paṭissutvā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya attadutiyo kusināraṃ pāvisi. Tena kho pana samayena kosinārakā mallā sandhāgāre sannipatitā honti teneva karaṇīyena. Atha kho āyasmā ānando yena kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ sandhāgāraṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ ārocesi – ‘parinibbuto, vāseṭṭhā, bhagavā, yassadāni kālaṃ maññathā’ti. Idamāyasmato ānandassa vacanaṃ sutvā mallā ca mallaputtā ca mallasuṇisā ca mallapajāpatiyo ca aghāvino dummanā cetodukkhasamappitā appekacce kese pakiriya kandanti, bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti, vivaṭṭanti – ‘‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antarahito’’ti.

226.Then the Venerable Anuruddha addressed the Venerable Ānanda: "Go, friend Ānanda, enter Kusinārā and announce to the Mallas of Kusinārā: 'The Blessed One, Vāseṭṭhas, has passed away into final Nibbāna. Now is the time as you think fit.'" "Yes, venerable sir," replied the Venerable Ānanda to the Venerable Anuruddha. Then, having dressed in the morning and taken his bowl and robe, accompanied by one other person, he entered Kusinārā. At that time, the Mallas of Kusinārā had gathered in the assembly hall for that very purpose. Then the Venerable Ānanda approached the assembly hall of the Mallas of Kusinārā and announced to them: "The Blessed One, Vāseṭṭhas, has passed away into final Nibbāna. Now is the time as you think fit." Hearing the Venerable Ānanda's words, the Mallas, their sons, daughters-in-law, and womenfolk were afflicted, saddened, their minds overwhelmed with the pain of grief. Some tore their hair and wept, some stretched out their arms and wailed, some fell prostrate as if cut down, rolling back and forth, crying: "Too soon has the Blessed One passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Sublime One passed away into final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Eye in the World vanished!"

## Buddhasarīrapūjā

### Veneration of the Buddha’s Body

227. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā purise āṇāpesuṃ – ‘‘tena hi, bhaṇe, kusinārāyaṃ gandhamālañca sabbañca tāḷāvacaraṃ sannipātethā’’ti. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā gandhamālañca sabbañca tāḷāvacaraṃ pañca ca dussayugasatāni ādāya yena upavattanaṃ mallānaṃ sālavanaṃ, yena bhagavato sarīraṃ tenupasaṅkamiṃsu; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavato sarīraṃ naccehi gītehi vāditehi mālehi gandhehi sakkarontā garuṃ karontā mānentā pūjentā celavitānāni karontā maṇḍalamāḷe paṭiyādentā ekadivasaṃ vītināmesuṃ.

227.Then the Mallas of Kusinārā ordered their men: “Friends, gather perfumes, garlands, and all kinds of music in Kusinārā.” Then the Mallas of Kusinārā, taking perfumes, garlands, all kinds of music, and five hundred pairs of cloths, went to the Mallas’ sal grove at Upavattana, where the Blessed One’s body was. Having gone there, they honored, respected, revered, and venerated the Blessed One’s body with dances, songs, music, garlands, and perfumes, making cloth canopies and preparing circular pavilions, and spent one day.

Atha kho kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘ativikālo kho ajja bhagavato sarīraṃ jhāpetuṃ, sve dāni mayaṃ bhagavato sarīraṃ jhāpessāmā’’ti. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā bhagavato sarīraṃ naccehi gītehi vāditehi mālehi gandhehi sakkarontā garuṃ karontā mānentā pūjentā celavitānāni karontā maṇḍalamāḷe paṭiyādentā dutiyampi divasaṃ vītināmesuṃ, tatiyampi divasaṃ vītināmesuṃ, catutthampi divasaṃ vītināmesuṃ, pañcamampi divasaṃ vītināmesuṃ, chaṭṭhampi divasaṃ vītināmesuṃ.

Then the Mallas of Kusinārā thought: “It is too late today to cremate the Blessed One’s body; tomorrow, then, we will cremate the Blessed One’s body.” Then the Mallas of Kusinārā, honoring, respecting, revering, and venerating the Blessed One’s body with dances, songs, music, garlands, and perfumes, making cloth canopies and preparing circular pavilions, spent the second day, the third day, the fourth day, the fifth day, and the sixth day.

Atha kho sattamaṃ divasaṃ kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘mayaṃ bhagavato sarīraṃ naccehi gītehi vāditehi mālehi gandhehi sakkarontā garuṃ karontā mānentā pūjentā dakkhiṇena dakkhiṇaṃ nagarassa haritvā bāhirena bāhiraṃ dakkhiṇato nagarassa bhagavato sarīraṃ jhāpessāmā’’ti.

Then, on the seventh day, the Mallas of Kusinārā had this thought: “Let us honor, respect, esteem, and venerate the Blessed One’s body with dances, songs, music, garlands, and perfumes. Then, carrying it southwards, through the southern part of the city, outside the outer walls, we will cremate the Blessed One’s body to the south of the city.”

228. Tena kho pana samayena aṭṭha mallapāmokkhā sīsaṃnhātā ahatāni vatthāni nivatthā ‘‘mayaṃ bhagavato sarīraṃ uccāressāmā’’ti na sakkonti uccāretuṃ. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā āyasmantaṃ anuruddhaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘ko nu kho, bhante anuruddha, hetu ko paccayo, yenime aṭṭha mallapāmokkhā sīsaṃnhātā ahatāni vatthāni nivatthā ‘mayaṃ bhagavato sarīraṃ uccāressāmā’ti na sakkonti uccāretu’’nti? ‘‘Aññathā kho, vāseṭṭhā, tumhākaṃ adhippāyo, aññathā devatānaṃ adhippāyo’’ti. ‘‘Kathaṃ pana, bhante, devatānaṃ adhippāyo’’ti? ‘‘Tumhākaṃ kho, vāseṭṭhā, adhippāyo – ‘mayaṃ bhagavato sarīraṃ naccehi gītehi vāditehi mālehi gandhehi sakkarontā garuṃ karontā mānentā pūjentā dakkhiṇena dakkhiṇaṃ nagarassa haritvā bāhirena bāhiraṃ dakkhiṇato nagarassa bhagavato sarīraṃ jhāpessāmā’ti; devatānaṃ kho, vāseṭṭhā, adhippāyo – ‘mayaṃ bhagavato sarīraṃ dibbehi naccehi gītehi vāditehi gandhehi sakkarontā garuṃ karontā mānentā pūjentā uttarena uttaraṃ nagarassa haritvā uttarena dvārena nagaraṃ pavesetvā majjhena majjhaṃ nagarassa haritvā puratthimena dvārena nikkhamitvā puratthimato nagarassa makuṭabandhanaṃ nāma mallānaṃ cetiyaṃ ettha bhagavato sarīraṃ jhāpessāmā’ti. ‘‘Yathā, bhante, devatānaṃ adhippāyo, tathā hotū’’ti.

228.Now at that time, eight leading Mallas, having bathed their heads and dressed in fresh clothes, said, “We will lift the Blessed One’s body,” but they were unable to lift it. Then the Mallas of Kusinārā said to Venerable Anuruddha: “What is the reason, Venerable Anuruddha, what is the cause, why these eight leading Mallas, having bathed their heads and dressed in fresh clothes, say, ‘We will lift the Blessed One’s body,’ but are unable to lift it?” “Your intention, Vāseṭṭhas, is one thing, the intention of the devas is another.” “But what, Venerable, is the intention of the devas?” “Your intention, Vāseṭṭhas, is this: ‘We will honor, respect, revere, and venerate the Blessed One’s body with dances, songs, music, garlands, and perfumes, and carrying it southwards, through the southern part of the city, outside the outer walls, we will cremate the Blessed One’s body to the south of the city.’ But the intention of the devas, Vāseṭṭhas, is this: ‘We will honor, respect, revere, and venerate the Blessed One’s body with divine dances, songs, music, and perfumes, and carrying it northwards, through the northern part of the city, entering the city by the northern gate, proceeding through the center of the city, and exiting by the eastern gate, we will cremate the Blessed One’s body at the Mallas’ shrine named Makutabandhana to the east of the city.’ ” “Let it be, Venerable, as the devas intend.”

229. Tena kho pana samayena kusinārā yāva sandhisamalasaṃkaṭīrā jaṇṇumattena odhinā mandāravapupphehi santhatā [saṇṭhitā (syā.)] hoti. Atha kho devatā ca kosinārakā ca mallā bhagavato sarīraṃ dibbehi ca mānusakehi ca naccehi gītehi vāditehi mālehi gandhehi sakkarontā garuṃ karontā mānentā pūjentā uttarena uttaraṃ nagarassa haritvā uttarena dvārena nagaraṃ pavesetvā majjhena majjhaṃ nagarassa haritvā puratthimena dvārena nikkhamitvā puratthimato nagarassa makuṭabandhanaṃ nāma mallānaṃ cetiyaṃ ettha ca bhagavato sarīraṃ nikkhipiṃsu.

229.At that time, Kusinārā was strewn knee-deep with mandārava flowers, right up to the joins in the walls, the filth drains, and the rubbish heaps. Then the devas and the Mallas of Kusinārā, honoring, respecting, revering, and venerating the Blessed One’s body with divine and human dances, songs, music, garlands, and perfumes, carried it northwards, through the northern part of the city, entered by the northern gate, proceeded through the center of the city, exited by the eastern gate, and placed the Blessed One’s body at the Mallas’ shrine named Makutabandhana, east of the city.

230. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘kathaṃ mayaṃ, bhante ānanda, tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjāmā’’ti? ‘‘Yathā kho, vāseṭṭhā, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjanti, evaṃ tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjitabba’’nti. ‘‘Kathaṃ pana, bhante ānanda, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjantī’’ti? ‘‘Rañño, vāseṭṭhā, cakkavattissa sarīraṃ ahatena vatthena veṭhenti, ahatena vatthena veṭhetvā vihatena kappāsena veṭhenti, vihatena kappāsena veṭhetvā ahatena vatthena veṭhenti. Etena upāyena pañcahi yugasatehi rañño cakkavattissa sarīraṃ veṭhetvā āyasāya teladoṇiyā pakkhipitvā aññissā āyasāya doṇiyā paṭikujjitvā sabbagandhānaṃ citakaṃ karitvā rañño cakkavattissa sarīraṃ jhāpenti. Cātumahāpathe rañño cakkavattissa thūpaṃ karonti. Evaṃ kho, vāseṭṭhā, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjanti. Yathā kho, vāseṭṭhā, rañño cakkavattissa sarīre paṭipajjanti, evaṃ tathāgatassa sarīre paṭipajjitabbaṃ. Cātumahāpathe tathāgatassa thūpo kātabbo. Tattha ye mālaṃ vā gandhaṃ vā cuṇṇakaṃ vā āropessanti vā abhivādessanti vā cittaṃ vā pasādessanti, tesaṃ taṃ bhavissati dīgharattaṃ hitāya sukhāyā’’ti. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā purise āṇāpesuṃ – ‘‘tena hi, bhaṇe, mallānaṃ vihataṃ kappāsaṃ sannipātethā’’ti.

230.Then the Mallas of Kusinārā said to Venerable Ānanda: “How, Venerable Ānanda, should we proceed with the Tathāgata’s body?” “As, Vāseṭṭhas, they proceed with the body of a wheel-turning monarch, so should you proceed with the Tathāgata’s body.” “But how, Venerable Ānanda, do they proceed with the body of a wheel-turning monarch?” “The body of a wheel-turning monarch, Vāseṭṭhas, is wrapped in new cloth, and having wrapped it in new cloth, they wrap it in carded cotton wool. Having wrapped it in carded cotton wool, they wrap it again in new cloth. In this way, the body of a wheel-turning monarch is wrapped in five hundred layers of cloth, then placed in an iron oil-vessel and covered with another iron vessel. A pyre of all kinds of fragrant woods is built, and the body of the wheel-turning monarch is cremated. A stupa is erected for the wheel-turning monarch at the four crossroads. Thus, Vāseṭṭhas, they proceed with the body of a wheel-turning monarch. As they proceed with the body of a wheel-turning monarch, so should you proceed with the Tathāgata’s body. A stupa for the Tathāgata should be built at the four crossroads. Those who there offer garlands or perfumes or powders, or pay homage, or inspire confidence in their minds—that will be for their long-term welfare and happiness.” Then the Mallas of Kusinārā ordered their men: “Friends, gather the Mallas’ carded cotton wool.”

Atha kho kosinārakā mallā bhagavato sarīraṃ ahatena vatthena veṭhetvā vihatena kappāsena veṭhesuṃ, vihatena kappāsena veṭhetvā ahatena vatthena veṭhesuṃ. Etena upāyena pañcahi yugasatehi bhagavato sarīraṃ veṭhetvā āyasāya teladoṇiyā pakkhipitvā aññissā āyasāya doṇiyā paṭikujjitvā sabbagandhānaṃ citakaṃ karitvā bhagavato sarīraṃ citakaṃ āropesuṃ.

Then the Mallas of Kusinārā wrapped the Blessed One’s body in new cloth, and having wrapped it in carded cotton wool, they wrapped it in new cloth. In this way, they wrapped the Blessed One’s body in five hundred layers, alternating new cloth and carded cotton wool, then placed it in an iron oil-vessel, which was covered with another iron vessel. They made a pyre of all kinds of fragrant woods and placed the Blessed One’s body upon it.

## Mahākassapattheravatthu

### The Story of Venerable Mahākassapa

231. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā mahākassapo pāvāya kusināraṃ addhānamaggappaṭippanno hoti mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ pañcamattehi bhikkhusatehi. Atha kho āyasmā mahākassapo maggā okkamma aññatarasmiṃ rukkhamūle nisīdi. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro ājīvako kusinārāya mandāravapupphaṃ gahetvā pāvaṃ addhānamaggappaṭippanno hoti. Addasā kho āyasmā mahākassapo taṃ ājīvakaṃ dūratova āgacchantaṃ, disvā taṃ ājīvakaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘apāvuso, amhākaṃ satthāraṃ jānāsī’’ti? ‘‘Āmāvuso, jānāmi, ajja sattāhaparinibbuto samaṇo gotamo. Tato me idaṃ mandāravapupphaṃ gahita’’nti. Tattha ye te bhikkhū avītarāgā appekacce bāhā paggayha kandanti, chinnapātaṃ papatanti, āvaṭṭanti, vivaṭṭanti – ‘‘atikhippaṃ bhagavā parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaṃ cakkhuṃ loke antarahito’’ti. Ye pana te bhikkhū vītarāgā, te satā sampajānā adhivāsenti – ‘‘aniccā saṅkhārā, taṃ kutettha labbhā’’ti.

231.At that time, Venerable Mahākassapa was traveling on the road from Pāvā to Kusinārā with a large company of about five hundred monks. Then, Venerable Mahākassapa left the road and sat down at the foot of a certain tree. At that time, a certain Ājīvaka was traveling on the road from Kusinārā to Pāvā, carrying a mandārava flower. Venerable Mahākassapa saw the Ājīvaka coming from a distance and asked him, "Friend, do you know our Teacher?" "Yes, friend, I know. The ascetic Gotama attained final Nibbāna seven days ago. That is why I took this mandārava flower." There, those monks who were not free from passion wept, raising their arms, collapsing as if cut down, rolling back and forth, crying, "Too soon has the Blessed One attained final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Fortunate One attained final Nibbāna! Too soon has the Eye in the world disappeared!" But those monks who were free from passion, mindful and fully aware, endured, reflecting: "All conditioned things are impermanent; how could it be otherwise?"

232. Tena kho pana samayena subhaddo nāma vuddhapabbajito tassaṃ parisāyaṃ nisinno hoti. Atha kho subhaddo vuddhapabbajito te bhikkhū etadavoca – ‘‘alaṃ, āvuso, mā socittha, mā paridevittha, sumuttā mayaṃ tena mahāsamaṇena. Upaddutā ca homa – ‘idaṃ vo kappati, idaṃ vo na kappatī’ti. Idāni pana mayaṃ yaṃ icchissāma, taṃ karissāma, yaṃ na icchissāma, na taṃ karissāmā’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā mahākassapo bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘alaṃ, āvuso, mā socittha, mā paridevittha. Nanu etaṃ, āvuso, bhagavatā paṭikacceva akkhātaṃ – ‘sabbeheva piyehi manāpehi nānābhāvo vinābhāvo aññathābhāvo’. Taṃ kutettha, āvuso, labbhā. ‘Yaṃ taṃ jātaṃ bhūtaṃ saṅkhataṃ palokadhammaṃ, taṃ tathāgatassāpi sarīraṃ mā palujjī’ti, netaṃ ṭhānaṃ vijjatī’’ti.

232.Now at that time, Subhadda, an old renunciant, was sitting in that assembly. Then Subhadda, the old renunciant, said this to the monks: "Enough, friends, do not grieve, do not lament. We are well rid of that great ascetic. We were harassed by him: 'This is permissible for you, this is not permissible for you.' But now we will do what we want, and we will not do what we do not want."Then Venerable Mahākassapa addressed the monks: "Enough, friends, do not grieve, do not lament. Has not the Blessed One declared this beforehand: 'Separation, disunion, and otherness are inevitable with all that is dear and beloved'? How could it be otherwise, friends? It is impossible that this should be: 'May the body of the Tathagata not disintegrate,' when it is something born, come into being, compounded, and subject to decay."

233. Tena kho pana samayena cattāro mallapāmokkhā sīsaṃnhātā ahatāni vatthāni nivatthā – ‘‘mayaṃ bhagavato citakaṃ āḷimpessāmā’’ti na sakkonti āḷimpetuṃ. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā āyasmantaṃ anuruddhaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘ko nu kho, bhante anuruddha, hetu ko paccayo, yenime cattāro mallapāmokkhā sīsaṃnhātā ahatāni vatthāni nivatthā – ‘mayaṃ bhagavato citakaṃ āḷimpessāmā’ti na sakkonti āḷimpetu’’nti? ‘‘Aññathā kho, vāseṭṭhā, devatānaṃ adhippāyo’’ti. ‘‘Kathaṃ pana, bhante, devatānaṃ adhippāyo’’ti? ‘‘Devatānaṃ kho, vāseṭṭhā, adhippāyo – ‘ayaṃ āyasmā mahākassapo pāvāya kusināraṃ addhānamaggappaṭippanno mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ pañcamattehi bhikkhusatehi. Na tāva bhagavato citako pajjalissati, yāvāyasmā mahākassapo bhagavato pāde sirasā na vandissatī’’’ti. ‘‘Yathā, bhante, devatānaṃ adhippāyo, tathā hotū’’ti.

233.At that time, four Malla chieftains, having bathed their heads and dressed in new clothes, thinking, "We will ignite the Blessed One's pyre," were unable to ignite it. Then the Mallas of Kusinārā said to Venerable Anuruddha, "Venerable Anuruddha, what is the reason, what is the cause, that these four Malla chieftains, having bathed their heads and dressed in new clothes, thinking, 'We will ignite the Blessed One's pyre,' are unable to do so?" "Vāseṭṭhas, the deities have a different intention." "But, Venerable, what is the intention of the deities?" "Vāseṭṭhas, the deities' intention is this: 'This Venerable Mahākassapa is traveling from Pāvā to Kusinārā on the road, accompanied by a large Saṅgha of bhikkhus, about five hundred bhikkhus in all. The Blessed One's pyre shall not blaze until Venerable Mahākassapa has bowed to the Blessed One's feet with his head.'" "Venerable, let it be as the deities intend."

234. Atha kho āyasmā mahākassapo yena kusinārā makuṭabandhanaṃ nāma mallānaṃ cetiyaṃ, yena bhagavato citako tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ cīvaraṃ katvā añjaliṃ paṇāmetvā tikkhattuṃ citakaṃ padakkhiṇaṃ katvā bhagavato pāde sirasā vandi. Tānipi kho pañcabhikkhusatāni ekaṃsaṃ cīvaraṃ katvā añjaliṃ paṇāmetvā tikkhattuṃ citakaṃ padakkhiṇaṃ katvā bhagavato pāde sirasā vandiṃsu. Vandite ca panāyasmatā mahākassapena tehi ca pañcahi bhikkhusatehi sayameva bhagavato citako pajjali.

234.Then the Venerable Mahākassapa went to the Mallas' shrine called Makuṭabandhana in Kusinārā, where the Blessed One's pyre was. Having approached, he arranged his robe over one shoulder, raised his joined hands in salutation, circumambulated the pyre three times, and bowed his head at the Blessed One's feet. Those five hundred monks also arranged their robes over one shoulder, raised their joined hands in salutation, circumambulated the pyre three times, and bowed their heads at the Blessed One's feet. And when the Venerable Mahākassapa and those five hundred monks had paid homage, the Blessed One's pyre ignited by itself.

235. Jhāyamānassa kho pana bhagavato sarīrassa yaṃ ahosi chavīti vā cammanti vā maṃsanti vā nhārūti vā lasikāti vā, tassa neva chārikā paññāyittha, na masi; sarīrāneva avasissiṃsu. Seyyathāpi nāma sappissa vā telassa vā jhāyamānassa neva chārikā paññāyati, na masi; evameva bhagavato sarīrassa jhāyamānassa yaṃ ahosi chavīti vā cammanti vā maṃsanti vā nhārūti vā lasikāti vā, tassa neva chārikā paññāyittha, na masi; sarīrāneva avasissiṃsu. Tesañca pañcannaṃ dussayugasatānaṃ dveva dussāni na ḍayhiṃsu yañca sabbaabbhantarimaṃ yañca bāhiraṃ. Daḍḍhe ca kho pana bhagavato sarīre antalikkhā udakadhārā pātubhavitvā bhagavato citakaṃ nibbāpesi. Udakasālatopi [udakaṃ sālatopi (sī. syā. kaṃ.)] abbhunnamitvā bhagavato citakaṃ nibbāpesi. Kosinārakāpi mallā sabbagandhodakena bhagavato citakaṃ nibbāpesuṃ. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā bhagavato sarīrāni sattāhaṃ sandhāgāre sattipañjaraṃ karitvā dhanupākāraṃ parikkhipāpetvā [parikkhipitvā (syā.)] naccehi gītehi vāditehi mālehi gandhehi sakkariṃsu garuṃ kariṃsu mānesuṃ pūjesuṃ.

235.And as the Blessed One's body was burning, whatever was skin, or hide, or flesh, or sinew, or fluid—no ashes or soot were seen; only the relics remained. Just as when ghee or oil is burning, no ashes or soot are seen, so too, as the Blessed One's body was burning, whatever was skin, or hide, or flesh, or sinew, or fluid—no ashes or soot were seen; only the relics remained. And of those five hundred pairs of cloths, only two cloths—the innermost and outermost—were not consumed. Then, when the Blessed One's body had been burned, a stream of water from the sky appeared and extinguished the pyre. A water spout also rose up from the sal trees, extinguishing the pyre. The Mallas of Kusinārā too extinguished the pyre with all kinds of fragrant water. Then the Mallas of Kusinārā kept the Blessed One's relics in their council hall, surrounded them with a lattice of spears, and enclosed them with a rampart of bows. For seven days, they honored, revered, esteemed, and venerated them with dance, song, music, garlands, and perfumes.

## Sarīradhātuvibhājanaṃ

### The Division of the Relics.

236. Assosi kho rājā māgadho ajātasattu vedehiputto – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho rājā māgadho ajātasattu vedehiputto kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesi – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo ahampi khattiyo, ahampi arahāmi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, ahampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmī’’ti.

236.King Ajātasattu, the Magadhan king, son of Queen Videhī, heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then King Ajātasattu, the Magadhan king, sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and I too am a noble. I too am worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. I too will build a stupa and a great monument for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Assosuṃ kho vesālikā licchavī – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho vesālikā licchavī kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesuṃ – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo mayampi khattiyā, mayampi arahāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, mayampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmā’’ti.

The Licchavis of Vesali heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Licchavis of Vesali sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and we too are nobles. We too are worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. We too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Assosuṃ kho kapilavatthuvāsī sakyā – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho kapilavatthuvāsī sakyā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesuṃ – ‘‘bhagavā amhākaṃ ñātiseṭṭho, mayampi arahāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, mayampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmā’’ti.

The Sakyans of Kapilavatthu heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Sakyans of Kapilavatthu sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was our foremost relative. We too are worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. We too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Assosuṃ kho allakappakā bulayo [thūlayo (syā.)] – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho allakappakā bulayo kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesuṃ – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo mayampi khattiyā, mayampi arahāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, mayampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmā’’ti.

The Bulis of Allakappa heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Bulis of Allakappa sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and we too are nobles. We too are worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. We too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Assosuṃ kho rāmagāmakā koḷiyā – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho rāmagāmakā koḷiyā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesuṃ – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo mayampi khattiyā, mayampi arahāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, mayampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmā’’ti.

The Koliyans of Rāmagāma heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Koliyans of Rāmagāma sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and we too are nobles. We too are worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. We too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Assosi kho veṭṭhadīpako brāhmaṇo – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho veṭṭhadīpako brāhmaṇo kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesi – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo ahaṃ pismi brāhmaṇo, ahampi arahāmi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, ahampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmī’’ti.

The Brahmin Veṭṭhadīpaka heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Brahmin Veṭṭhadīpaka sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and I too am a brahmin. I too am worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. I too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Assosuṃ kho pāveyyakā mallā – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho pāveyyakā mallā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesuṃ – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo mayampi khattiyā, mayampi arahāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, mayampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmā’’ti.

The Mallas of Pāvā heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Mallas of Pāvā sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and we too are nobles. We too are worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. We too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.”

Evaṃ vutte kosinārakā mallā te saṅghe gaṇe etadavocuṃ – ‘‘bhagavā amhākaṃ gāmakkhette parinibbuto, na mayaṃ dassāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāga’’nti.

When this was said, the Mallas of Kusinārā said to those assemblies and groups: “The Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna in our village territory. We will not give a share of the Blessed One’s relics.”

237. Evaṃ vutte doṇo brāhmaṇo te saṅghe gaṇe etadavoca –

237.When this was said, the brahmin Doṇa said this to those assemblies and groups:

‘‘Suṇantu bhonto mama ekavācaṃ,Amhāka [chandānurakkhaṇatthaṃ niggahītalopo]; Buddho ahu khantivādo;Na hi sādhu yaṃ uttamapuggalassa,Sarīrabhāge siyā sampahāro.

“Listen, sirs, to this one word of mine: Our Buddha was an advocate of forbearance. It is not proper that there should be conflict over the bodily remains of the supreme person.”

Sabbeva bhonto sahitā samaggā,Sammodamānā karomaṭṭhabhāge;Vitthārikā hontu disāsu thūpā,Bahū janā cakkhumato pasannā’’ti.

“Let all of you, sirs, united and in harmony, rejoicing together, let us make eight shares; May stupas be widespread in all directions, so that many people may have faith in the One with Vision.”

238. ‘‘Tena hi, brāhmaṇa, tvaññeva bhagavato sarīrāni aṭṭhadhā samaṃ savibhattaṃ vibhajāhī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bho’’ti kho doṇo brāhmaṇo tesaṃ saṅghānaṃ gaṇānaṃ paṭissutvā bhagavato sarīrāni aṭṭhadhā samaṃ suvibhattaṃ vibhajitvā te saṅghe gaṇe etadavoca – ‘‘imaṃ me bhonto tumbaṃ dadantu ahampi tumbassa thūpañca mahañca karissāmī’’ti. Adaṃsu kho te doṇassa brāhmaṇassa tumbaṃ.

238.“Then, Brahmin, you yourself divide the Blessed One’s relics into eight equal and well-divided shares.” “Very well, sirs,” replied the brahmin Doṇa. Having assented to those assemblies and groups, he divided the Blessed One’s relics into eight equal and well-divided shares. Then he addressed those assemblies and groups: “Sirs, give me this urn. I too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the urn.” They gave the urn to the brahmin Doṇa.

Assosuṃ kho pippalivaniyā [pipphalivaniyā (syā.)] moriyā – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusinārāyaṃ parinibbuto’’ti. Atha kho pippalivaniyā moriyā kosinārakānaṃ mallānaṃ dūtaṃ pāhesuṃ – ‘‘bhagavāpi khattiyo mayampi khattiyā, mayampi arahāma bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgaṃ, mayampi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca karissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Natthi bhagavato sarīrānaṃ bhāgo, vibhattāni bhagavato sarīrāni. Ito aṅgāraṃ harathā’’ti. Te tato aṅgāraṃ hariṃsu [āhariṃsu (syā. ka.)].

The Moriyas of Pippalivana heard: “Indeed, the Blessed One has attained final Nibbāna at Kusinārā.” Then the Moriyas of Pippalivana sent a messenger to the Mallas of Kusinārā, saying: “The Blessed One was a noble, and we too are nobles. We too are worthy of a share of the Blessed One’s relics. We too will build a stupa and a great celebration for the Blessed One’s relics.” [The Mallas replied:] “There is no share of the Blessed One’s relics left. The Blessed One’s relics have been divided. Take the embers from here.” So they took the embers from there.

## Dhātuthūpapūjā

### Veneration of the Stupas of Relics.

239. Atha kho rājā māgadho ajātasattu vedehiputto rājagahe bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akāsi. Vesālikāpi licchavī vesāliyaṃ bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Kapilavatthuvāsīpi sakyā kapilavatthusmiṃ bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Allakappakāpi bulayo allakappe bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Rāmagāmakāpi koḷiyā rāmagāme bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Veṭṭhadīpakopi brāhmaṇo veṭṭhadīpe bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akāsi. Pāveyyakāpi mallā pāvāyaṃ bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Kosinārakāpi mallā kusinārāyaṃ bhagavato sarīrānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Doṇopi brāhmaṇo tumbassa thūpañca mahañca akāsi. Pippalivaniyāpi moriyā pippalivane aṅgārānaṃ thūpañca mahañca akaṃsu. Iti aṭṭha sarīrathūpā navamo tumbathūpo dasamo aṅgārathūpo. Evametaṃ bhūtapubbanti.

239.Then King Ajātasattu of Magadha, son of the Videhī, built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Rājagaha. The Licchavis of Vesālī also built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Vesālī. The Sakyans of Kapilavatthu built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Kapilavatthu. The Bulis of Allakappa built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Allakappa. The Koliyas of Rāmagāma built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Rāmagāma. The brahmin Veṭṭhadīpaka built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Veṭṭhadīpa. The Mallas of Pāvā built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Pāvā. The Mallas of Kusinārā built a stupa for the Blessed One’s relics and held a great festival at Kusinārā. The brahmin Doṇa built a stupa for the measuring vessel and held a great festival. The Moriyas of Pipphalivana built a stupa for the embers and held a great festival at Pipphalivana. Thus, there were eight stupas for the relics, the ninth was the stupa for the measuring vessel, and the tenth was the stupa for the embers. So it was in the past.

240. Aṭṭhadoṇaṃ cakkhumato sarīraṃ, sattadoṇaṃ jambudīpe mahenti.

240.The body of the One with Vision is eight measures; seven measures are venerated in Jambudīpa.

Ekañca doṇaṃ purisavaruttamassa, rāmagāme nāgarājā maheti.

And one measure of the foremost of men, the Nāga king venerates at Rāmagāma.

Ekāhi dāṭhā tidivehi pūjitā, ekā pana gandhārapure mahīyati;Kāliṅgarañño vijite punekaṃ, ekaṃ pana nāgarājā maheti.

One tooth is worshipped by the devas in Tāvatiṃsa, another is honored in the city of Gandhāra; yet another is in the realm of the Kalinga king, and one is venerated by the Nāga king.

Tasseva tejena ayaṃ vasundharā,Āyāgaseṭṭhehi mahī alaṅkatā;Evaṃ imaṃ cakkhumato sarīraṃ,Susakkataṃ sakkatasakkatehi.

By his very splendor, this earth is adorned, the ground embellished with the foremost objects of worship. Thus, this body of the One with Vision is well-honored, honored by those worthy of honor.

Devindanāgindanarindapūjito,Manussindaseṭṭhehi tatheva pūjito;Taṃ vandatha [taṃ taṃ vandatha (syā.)] pañjalikā labhitvā,Buddho have kappasatehi dullabhoti.

Worshipped by lords of devas, lords of nāgas, and lords of men, likewise honored by the foremost of human lords. Having obtained (this opportunity), venerate him with joined palms, for indeed, a Buddha is hard to find even in hundreds of aeons.

Cattālīsa samā dantā, kesā lomā ca sabbaso;Devā hariṃsu ekekaṃ, cakkavāḷaparamparāti.

Forty teeth were equal, and all the hairs and body hairs; the devas took them away one by one, from universe to universe.

## Mahāparinibbānasuttaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ tatiyaṃ.

### The Great Discourse on the Final Nibbāna, the third section, is concluded.
